Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">27</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">6670</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">6676</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201502864</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D27%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D6670-6676%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DX.%2BH.%2BRui%26author%3DW.%2BSun%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26author%3DQ.%2BYan%26title%3DAn%2BAdvanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BComposed%2Bof%2BCarbon%2BCoated%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2Bin%2Ba%2BPorous%2BGraphene%2BNetwork%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201502864&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11238&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201502864&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Advanced Sodium-Ion Battery Composed of Carbon Coated Na3V2(PO4)3 in a Porous Graphene Network</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rui, Xianhong; Sun, Wenping; Wu, Chao; Yu, Yan; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6670-6676</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, to create efficient charge transfer, we propose a 3D hierarchical meso- and macroporous NVP-based hybrid cathode concept with connected Na ion/electron pathways for ultrafast charge and discharge NIBs, consisting of NVP nanocrystals coated with amorphous carbon and then wrapped by reduced graphene oxide nanosheets (abbreviated as NVP@C@rGO).  Specifically, i) the small nanograins shorten the lengths of solid-state Na ion diffusion, ii) the macro/mesopore network enables rapid ion transport and buffers the strain during repeated Na+ extn./insertion to maintain the structural integrity, iii) highly conductive amorphous coating carbon and rGO nanosheets facilitate fast electron transfer within the electrode and to the current collector.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Charge carriers in rechargeable batteries: Na ions vs. Li ions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Sung You; Kim, Youngjin; Park, Yuwon; Choi, Aram; Choi, Nam-Soon; Lee, Kyu Tae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2067-2081</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  We discuss the similarities and dissimilarities of sodium- and lithium-ion batteries in terms of neg. and pos. electrodes.  Compared to the comprehensive body of work on lithium-ion batteries, research on sodium-ion batteries is still at the germination stage.  Since both sodium and lithium are alkali metals, they share similar chem. properties including ionicity, electronegativity and electrochem. reactivity.  They accordingly have comparable synthetic protocols and electrochem. performances, which indicates that sodium-ion batteries can be successfully developed based on previously applied approaches or methods in the lithium counterpart.  The electrode materials in Li-ion batteries provide the best library for research on Na-ion batteries because many Na-ion insertion hosts have their roots in Li-ion insertion hosts.  However, the larger size and different bonding characteristics of sodium ions influence the thermodn. and/or kinetic properties of sodium-ion batteries, which leads to unexpected behavior in electrochem. performance and reaction mechanism, compared to lithium-ion batteries.  This perspective provides a comparative overview of the major developments in the area of pos. and neg. electrode materials in both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries in the past decade.  Highlighted are concepts in solid state chem. and electrochem. that have provided new opportunities for tailored design that can be extended to many different electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHBS0wIkomorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMBE_g3pZxcw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWmtL%252FE&amp;md5=023136cc0e5ed94e18ce0d526a0000a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1038/nnano.2015.194"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pasta, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorene-Graphene Hybrid Material as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMBE_g3pZxcw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201404549"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Ultrastable Anode for Long-Life Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Ultrastable Anode for Long-Life Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Haijun; Ren, Yang; Xiao, Dongdong; Guo, Shaohua; Zhu, Yanbei; Qian, Yumin; Gu, Lin; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are important alternative energy storage devices that have recently come again into focus for the development of large-scale energy storage devices because sodium is an abundant and low-cost material. Na2/3Co1/3Ti2/3O2, exhibits outstanding cycle stability (∼84.84% capacity retention after 3000 cycles, very small decrease in the vol.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mechanistic Insight into the Stability of HfO2-Coated MoS2 Nanosheet Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ahmed, Bilal; Anjum, Dalaver H.; Hedhili, Mohamed N.; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is demonstrated for the first time that surface passivation of 2D nanosheets of MoS2 by an ultrathin and uniform layer of HfO2 can significantly improve the cyclic performance of sodium ion batteries.  After 50 charge/discharge cycles, bare MoS2 and HfO2 coated MoS2 electrodes deliver the specific capacity of 435 and 636 mAh g-1, resp., at c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  These results imply that batteries using HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes retain 91% of the initial capacity; in contrast, bare MoS2 anodes retain only 63%.  Also, HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes show one of the highest reported capacity values for MoS2.  Cyclic voltammetry and XPS results suggest that HfO2 does not take part in electrochem. reaction.  The mechanism of capacity retention with HfO2 coating is explained by ex situ transmission electron microscope imaging and elec. impedance spectroscopy.  HfO2 acts as a passivation layer at the anode/electrolyte interface and prevents structural degrdn. during charge/discharge process.  Moreover, the amorphous nature of HfO2 allows facile diffusion of Na ions.  These results clearly show the potential of HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes, which performance is significantly higher than previous reports where bulk MoS2 or composites of MoS2 with carbonaceous materials are used.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqG15e3D2W7WLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQG9os1UT_zQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXpvVegsbo%253D&amp;md5=2b2108aa242063c6214974eaf43cfbb4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1149/1.1393348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stevens, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahn, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity Anode Materials for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. A.; Dahn, J. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. techniques have been used to study the reversible insertion of sodium into hard-carbon host structures at room temp.  In this paper we compare these results with those for lithium insertion in the same materials and demonstrate the presence of similar alkali metal insertion mechanisms in both cases.  Despite the gravimetric capacities being lower for sodium than lithium insertion, we have achieved a reversible sodium capacity of 300 mAh/g, close to that for lithium insertion in graphitic carbon anode materials.  Such materials may therefore be useful as anodes in rechargeable sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpm125w9mEFSbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQG9os1UT_zQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3cXisVygtL0%253D&amp;md5=7480ac0a7bc2620ce565b1c21f1e2463</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.02.022"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kretschmer, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sn@CNT Nanopillars Grown Perpendicularly on Carbon Paper: a Novel Free-Standing Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">13</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">208</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">217</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sn@CNT nanopillars grown perpendicularly on carbon paper: A novel free-standing anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Xiuqiang; Kretschmer, Katja; Zhang, Jinqiang; Sun, Bing; Su, Dawei; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">208-217</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have attracted extensive interest for energy storage and conversion as an alternative to lithium-ion batteries.  The development of advanced electrode materials is important for the implementation of sodium-ion batteries into practical applications.  Herein, we developed a facile soaking-chem. vapor deposition method to grow core-sheath structured Sn@CNT nanopillar arrays on carbon paper with a unique 3D hierarchical architecture as free-standing electrode for sodium-ion batteries.  The electrode achieved a reversible capacity of 887 μA h cm-2 in the first cycle and good cyclability extending to 100 cycles.  The electrode also demonstrated a promising rate capability, which is suitable for high power applications.  We also assembled prototype Na-ion full cells, consisting of the as-prepd. free-standing Sn@CNT@carbon paper anode and Na0.80Li0.12Ni0.22Mn0.66O2 cathode.  The full sodium-ion battery can power LED lights.  This work is expected to inspire the development of sustainable sodium-ion batteries for energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGozaFfJuwFGzLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQG9os1UT_zQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS2 to Orthorhombic-SnS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Tengfei; Pang, Wei Kong; Zhang, Chaofeng; Yang, Jianping; Chen, Zhixin; Liu, Hua Kun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8323-8333</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWHE3xEPCjvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQG9os1UT_zQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Probing the Failure Mechanism of SnO2 Nanowires for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gu, Meng; Kushima, Akihiro; Shao, Yuyan; Zhang, Ji-Guang; Liu, Jun; Browning, Nigel D.; Li, Ju; Wang, Chongmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Non-lithium metals such as Na have attracted attention as a potential charge carrying ion for rechargeable batteries.  Using in situ TEM in combination with d. functional theory calcns., the authors probed the structural and chem. evolution of SnO2 nanowire anodes in Na-ion batteries and compared them quant. with results from Li-ion batteries.  Upon Na insertion into SnO2, a displacement reaction occurs, giving amorphous NaxSn nanoparticles dispersed in Na2O matrix.  With further Na insertion, the NaxSn crystd. into Na15Sn4 (x = 3.75).  Upon extn. of Na (de-sodiation), the NaxSn transforms to Sn nanoparticles.  Assocd. with the de-alloying, pores form, leading to a structure of Sn particles confined in a hollow matrix of Na2O.  These pores greatly increase elec. impedance, therefore accounting for the poor cyclability of SnO2.  DFT calcns. indicate that Na+ diffuses 30 times slower than Li+ in SnO2, in agreement with in situ TEM measurement.  Insertion of Na can chemomechanically soften the reaction product to a greater extent than in lithiation.  Therefore, in contrast to the lithiation of SnO2 significantly less dislocation plasticity was seen ahead of the sodiation front.  This direct comparison of the results from Na and Li highlights the crit. role of ionic size and electronic structure of different ionic species on the charge/discharge rate and failure mechanisms in these batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxbnVD4FT9W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQG9os1UT_zQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFels7zP&amp;md5=3eeb24d9885b1c825918e689b7adbbb2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201305638"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Woo, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mok, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ryu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oh, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Phosphide as a Promising Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the abundance and low cost of sodium-contg. precursors ambient temp. sodium ion batteries are promising for large scale grid storage.  The low m.p. of Na (97.7 °C) compared to 180.6 °C for Li represents a significant safety hazard for the use of Na metal anodes at ambient temps., which emphasizes the need for scientists and engineers to identify, design and develop new neg. electrodes for Na-ion batteries.  The identification of a suitable neg. electrode is a crucial challenge for any further successful development of new cells, and to date efficient and competitive neg. electrodes for NaB are still very rare.  In this work we demonstrate that NiP3 could be a good challenger for this purpose.  NiP3 based electrodes are evaluated as neg. electrode materials for Li-ion batteries (LiB) and Na-ion batteries (NaB).  The study of the reaction mechanism reveals the formation of a phase of compn. close to Li3P and Na3P embedding Ni nanoparticles as the final reaction product after a full discharge.  While the direct conversion of NiP3 into Na3P is identified for the reaction vs. Na, it is still unclear whether an amorphous phase exists during the first discharge for the reaction vs. Li before the conversion.  Furthermore, thanks to the CM-cellulose/carbon black (CMC/CB) electrode formulation, the NiP3 electrode possesses a very promising capacity with a reversible storage capacity higher than 1000 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles for LiB and 900 mA h g-1 after 15 cycles for NaB, which represents one of the highest capacities ever sustained in Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOUBqz1xXoSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lio_ncu2ETGQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpslGjug%253D%253D&amp;md5=1e5512e9a0282ca35cdf95497825a466</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA09867J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ye, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Iron-Based Sodium-Ion Full Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries have been an active area of research over the past several years.  While a great deal of attention is now focused on the development and evaluation of single electrode materials, much less is paid to their combined performance in full batteries.  Most full batteries currently available suffer from rapid capacity fading under extended cycling.  In this study, we prep. ultra-small, poorly cryst. FeOx nanoparticles supported on carbon nanotubes as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It exhibits excellent half-cell performances; and, when combined with a Prussian blue cathode material, it leads to iron-based full batteries.  Our prototypes have a working voltage of ∼2 V, specific energy d. of ∼136 W h kg-1 and, most impressively, outstanding cycling stability at both low and high current rates with negligible capacity loss.  Owing to their low material and fabrication cost, long cycle life and high efficiency, we believe that these iron-based sodium-ion batteries would be highly appealing toward the stationary energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGolrxMNOb7GMrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lio_ncu2ETGQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitVyqsbzF&amp;md5=317f81b31e1e8d8b0c5f729fd16dbc57</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1021/cm025556v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alcántara, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jaraba, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lavela, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tirado, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiCo<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Spinel: First Report on a Transition Metal Oxide for the Negative Electrode of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Micelle-templated ordered mesoporous nickel-cobalt carbonates and oxides are fabricated using a metal nitrate-citric acid strategy, which avoids the hydrolysis and aging requirements assocd. with sol-gel chem.  A series of mesoporous NixCo(3-x)(CO3)y and NixCo(3-x)O4 films with varying Ni-Co compns. and 14 ± 4 nm mesopores are fabricated with the same block copolymer template.  AFM and GISAXS anal. indicates that the mesostructure is maintained through the formation of the carbonate and oxide, while GIXD profiles confirm formation of pure spinel phases of semi-cryst. NixCo(3-x)O4.  The micelle templated mesopores are interconnected and provide transport paths for the electrolyte to minimize the solid-state diffusion requirements assocd. with battery electrodes.  These materials exhibit good performance as sodium ion battery anodes even at high current densities of 4 A g-1.  Amongst the mixed-metal oxides, Ni2CoO4 exhibits the highest specific capacity of 239 mA h g-1 after galvanostatic cycling at a c.d. of 1 A g-1 for 10 cycles.  The superior performance of Ni2CoO4 at high rates is attributed to the high surface area and short ion-diffusion paths of the nanoporous anode architecture, while the higher nickel content in the mixed metal oxide provides enhanced stability during oxide formation along with enhanced electronic cond., leading to improved cycling stability of the anode.  This micelle template metal nitrate-citric acid method enables new possibilities for fabricating variety of ordered mesoporous mixed-metal carbonates and oxides that could be used in a wide range of applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOj35oA0taBbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhoYTK-o7GMEQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFWhtLzJ&amp;md5=18622fb821b1321e7d25704a26915e57</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1038/nmat1368"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Arico, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bruce, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Scrosati, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Schalkwijk, W.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructured Materials for Advanced Energy Conversion and Storage Devices</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Nanomaterials offer unique properties or combinations of properties as electrodes and electrolytes in a range of energy devices.  This article describes some recent developments in the discovery of nanoelectrolytes and nanoelectrodes for lithium batteries, fuel cells and supercapacitors.  The advantages and disadvantages of the nanoscale in materials design for such devices are highlighted.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrfGEM7psSXRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhoYTK-o7GMEQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXjsl2msr0%253D&amp;md5=07521379308cfee3ceb1932ad7637a50</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1149/2.054303jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mohamed, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Whitacre, F.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Microwave Synthesized NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as an Aqueous Sodium-Ion Negative Electrode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microwave synthesized NaTi2(PO4)3 as an aqueous sodium-ion negative electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Wei; Mohamed, Alex; Whitacre, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-coated NaTi2(PO4)3 was successfully synthesized by a rapid microwave-assisted method and was found to have promising electrochem. function in a neutral pH Na2SO4 aq. electrolyte.  The effects of various processing parameters, including precursor ball mill time, microwave irradn. parameters, and graphite precursor concn., on the phys. and electrochem. properties of the synthesized NaTi2(PO4)3 were investigated.  To further study electrochem. performance, a full test cell consisting of NaTi2(PO4)3/1M Na2SO4/Na0.44MnO2 was assembled.  The highest discharge specific capacity obtained for this material was 85 mA-h/g.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin nickel oxide nanosheets for enhanced sodium and lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Wenping; Rui, Xianhong; Zhu, Jixin; Yu, Linghui; Zhang, Yu; Xu, Zhichuan; Madhavi, Srinivasan; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">274</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Outstanding Na and Li storage capability is successfully demonstrated in ultrathin NiO nanosheets (4-5 nm in thickness) synthesized via a facile solvothermal process followed by annealing in air.  For Na storage, the NiO nanosheets deliver a high reversible specific capacity of 299 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 1 A g-1, and the capacity still remains up to 154 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1.  Upon charge/discharge cycling, the specific capacity maintains to be ≤266 mA h g-1 during the 100th cycle at 1 A g-1.  Such Na storage capability of NiO nanosheets is by far one of the best reported for transition metal oxides.  For Li storage, the cell achieves a high reversible specific capacity of 1242 and 250 mA h g-1 at 0.2 and 15 A g-1, resp.  The capacity for Li storage maintains to be 851 mA h g-1 during the 170th cycle at 2 A g-1.  Ultrathin NiO nanosheets are highly attractive for fast Na/Li diffusion with high-rate capability for rechargeable Na-ion batteries (SIBs) and Li-ion batteries (LIBs).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-6AFm_88BSLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhoYTK-o7GMEQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVamtr3I&amp;md5=245647026fd3b90db2f4ffdae97cb290</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1038/srep22432"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cho, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-ion Storage Performances of FeSe<sub>x</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Hollow Nanoparticles-Decorated Reduced Graphene Oxide Balls Prepared by Nanoscale Kirkendall Diffusion</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion Storage Performances of FeSex and Fe2O3 Hollow Nanoparticles-Decorated Reduced Graphene Oxide Balls prepared by Nanoscale Kirkendall Diffusion Process</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Gi Dae; Cho, Jung Sang; Lee, Jung-Kul; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Uniquely structured FeSex-reduced graphene oxide (rGO) composite powders, in which hollow FeSex nanoparticles are uniformly distributed throughout the rGO matrix, were prepd. by spray pyrolysis applying the nanoscale Kirkendall diffusion process.  Iron oxide-rGO composite powders were transformed into FeSex-rGO composite powders by a two-step post-treatment process.  Metallic Fe nanocrystals formed during the first-step post-treatment process were transformed into hollow FeSex nanoparticles during the selenization process.  The FeSex-rGO composite powders had mixed crystal structures of FeSe and FeSe2 phases.  A rGO content of 33% was estd. from the TG anal. of the FeSex-rGO composite powders.  The FeSex-rGO composite powders had superior sodium-ion storage properties compared to those of the Fe2O3-rGO composite powders with similar morphol. characteristics.  The discharge capacities of the FeSex- and Fe2O3-rGO composite powders for the 200th cycle at a const. c.d. of 0.3 A g-1 were 434 and 174 mA h g-1, resp.  The FeSex-rGO composite powders had a high discharge capacity of 311 mA h g-1 for the 1000th cycle at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr2yGg7A95VurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhoYTK-o7GMEQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjsFentLk%253D&amp;md5=cea175f32bd0b3a76270f67c7ec83b56</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.02.071"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Valvo, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Philippe, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lindgren, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tai, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Edström, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Insight into the Processes Controlling the Electrochemical Reactions of Nanostructured Iron Oxide Electrodes in Li- and Na-Half Cells</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous TiO2 Nanotube Anode for Rechargeable Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Hui; Slater, Michael D.; Balasubramanian, Mahalingam; Johnson, Christopher S.; Rajh, Tijana</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an attractive alternative to lithium-ion batteries that alleviate problems with lithium availability and cost.  Despite several studies of cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries involving layered oxide materials, there are few low-voltage metal oxide anodes capable of operating sodium ion reversibly at room temp.  We have synthesized amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube electrodes directly grown on current collectors without binders and additives to use as an anode for sodium-ion batteries.  We find that only amorphous large diam. nanotubes (&gt;80 nm I.D.) can support electrochem. cycling with sodium ions.  These electrodes maximize their capacity in operando and reach reversible capacity of 150 mA-h/g in 15 cycles.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solid-State Fabrication of SnS2/C Nanospheres for High-Performance Sodium Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jingjing; Luo, Chao; Mao, Jianfeng; Zhu, Yujie; Fan, Xiulin; Gao, Tao; Mignerey, Alice C.; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin disulfide (SnS2) has emerged as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (NIBs) due to its unique layered structure, high theor. capacity, and low cost.  Conventional SnS2 nanomaterials are normally synthesized using hydrothermal method, which is time-consuming and difficult to scale up for mass prodn.  In this study, we develop a simple solid-state reaction method, in which the carbon-coated SnS2 (SnS2/C) anode materials were synthesized by annealing metallic Sn, sulfur powder, and polyacrylonitrile in a sealed vacuum glass tube.  The SnS2/C nanospheres with unique layered structure exhibit a high reversible capacity of 660 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 and maintain at 570 mAh g-1 for 100 cycles with a degrdn. rate of 0.14% per cycle, demonstrating one of the best cycling performances in all reported SnS2/C anodes for NIBs to date.  The superior cycling stability of SnS2/C electrode is attributed to the stable nanosphere morphol. and structural integrity during charge/discharge cycles as evidenced by ex situ characterization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWDnHlGxRZbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-i4xYG6kZtA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXot1egtr8%253D&amp;md5=85467db519989a8e264fe006526323b3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201503015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A rationally designed dual role anode material for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries: case study of eco-friendly Fe3O4</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hariharan, Srirama; Saravanan, Kuppan; Ramar, Vishwanathan; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2945-2953</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Identifying dual role electrode materials capable of storing both lithium and sodium are thought to be highly relevant, as these materials could find potential applications simultaneously in lithium- and sodium-ion batteries.  In this regard, the concept of dual alkali storage is demonstrated in Fe3O4 anode material undergoing conversion reaction.  To enable improved storage, a rational active material and electrode design is proposed.  Accordingly, the following features were simultaneously incorporated into the design: (a) an optimal particle size, (b) a conducting matrix, (c) adequately large active material surface area and (d) strong electrode material-current collector integrity.  Electrodes incorporating this rational design exhibit excellent high-rate performance and impressive cyclability during lithium storage.  For instance, Fe3O4 electrodes deliver a charge capacity of 950 mA-h/g at 1.2C (∼2.6 times higher than graphite and 5.4 times higher than Li4Ti5O12).  Further, these electrodes show no signs of capacity fade even up to 1100 cycles.  Impressively, the cells could also be charged-discharged to 65% of their theor. capacity in just 5 min or 12C (11.11 A/g).  The rate performance and cyclability of lithium storage achieved here are amongst the highest reported values in the literature for the conversion reaction in Fe3O4.  Besides lithium storage, the dual role of this anode is shown by demonstrating its sodium storage ability by conversion reaction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq1Ci_Jjiz4hrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-i4xYG6kZtA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvVChu70%253D&amp;md5=3227d1451a01a4a00d2e9d504da1dc9e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b04178"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kalubarme, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon Encapsulated Tin Oxide Nanocomposites: An Efficient Anode for High Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon Encapsulated Tin Oxide Nanocomposites: An Efficient Anode for High Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kalubarme, Ramchandra S.; Lee, Jae-Young; Park, Chan-Jin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">31</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17226-17237</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The major obstacle in realizing sodium (Na)-ion batteries (NIBs) is the absence of suitable neg. electrodes.  This is because graphite, a com. well known anode material for lithium-ion batteries, cannot be utilized as an insertion host for Na ions due to its large ionic size.  In this study, a simple and cost-effective hydrothermal method to prep. carbon coated tin oxide (SnO2) nanostructures as an efficient anode material for NIBs was reported as a function of the solvent used.  A single phase SnO2 resulted for the ethanol solvent, while a blend of SnO and SnO2 resulted for the DI water and ethylene glycol solvents.  The elemental mapping in the transmission electron microscopy confirmed the presence of carbon coating on the SnO2 nanoparticles.  In cell tests, the anodes of carbon coated SnO2 prepd. in ethanol solvent exhibited stable cycling performance and attained a capacity of about 514 mAh g-1 on the first charge.  With the help of the conductive carbon coating, the SnO2 delivers more capacity at high rates: 304 mAh g-1 at the 1 C rate, 213 mAh g-1 at the 2 C rate and 133 mAh g-1 at the 5 C rate.  The excellent cyclability and high rate capability are the result of the formation of a mixed conducting network and uniform carbon coating on the SnO2 nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoqatmxHHS-GLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-i4xYG6kZtA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFyqs7zL&amp;md5=f5816e29156cc8b7ab64982328e0b5a2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b06590"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ Synthesis of MnS Hollow Microspheres on Reduced Graphene Oxide Sheets as High-Capacity and Long-Life Anodes for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Synthesis of MnS Hollow Microspheres on Reduced Graphene Oxide Sheets as High-Capacity and Long-Life Anodes for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xijun; Ji, Shaomin; Gu, Mingzhe; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20957-20964</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Uniform MnS hollow microspheres in situ crystd. on reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanosheets via a facile hydrothermal method.  The MnS/RGO composite material was used as the anode for Na-ion batteries for the first time and exhibited excellent cycling performance, superior specific capacity, and great cycle stability and rate capability for both Li- and Na-ion batteries.  Compared with nonencapsulated pure MnS hollow microspheres, these MnS/RGO nanocomposites demonstrated excellent charge-discharge stability and long cycle life.  Li-ion storage testing revealed that these MnS/RGO nanocomposites deliver high discharge-charge capacities of 640 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 400 cycles and 830 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 after 100 cycles.  The MnS/RGO nanocomposites even retained a specific capacity of 308 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 after 125 cycles as the anode for Na-ion batteries.  The outstanding electrochem. performance of the MnS/RGO composite attributed to the RGO nanosheets greatly improved the electronic cond. and efficiently mitigated the stupendous vol. expansion during the progress of charge and discharge.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqgyxM_04H9CLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-i4xYG6kZtA"> &gt;&gt; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A High-Rate and Ultralong-Life Sodium-Ion Battery Based on NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Nanocubes with Synergistic Coating of Carbon and Rutile TiO<sub>2</sub></span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Small</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">11</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3744</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3749</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High-Rate and Ultralong-Life Sodium-Ion Battery Based on NaTi2(PO4)3 Nanocubes with Synergistic Coating of Carbon and Rutile TiO2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Jie; Wang, Hua; Hu, Pengfei; Qi, Juanjuan; Guo, Lin; Wang, Lihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Highly regular NaTi2(PO4)3 nanocubes with synergistic nano-coating of rutile TiO2 and carbon was synthesized as electrode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The C/NTP-RT electrode exhibits high-rate and ultralong-life performance simultaneously, e.g., a superior capacity of 83.5 mA h g-1 at a high rate of 10 C and a cyclic capacity retention of 89.3% after 10 000 cycles.  The presented cyclability and stability is superior to most of previous reports, and bridge the gap between traditional supercapacitors and rechargeable sodium-ion batteries.  Addnl., this electrode architecture can be up-scaled and thus should hold a position in the future low-cost, high-rate and ultralong-life next-generation energy storage devices.  The nano-coating of rutile TiO2 improves surface stability as well as specific capacity of NaTi2(PO4)3 nanocubes, and the further coating of carbon provides enhanced rate capability.  Thus, besides the attractive electrochem. performance achieved here, this finding also highlights the importance of synergistic nano-coating manipulation for optimizing electrode materials for rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqUeFDW2NegUbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh_O28Qwd46Jw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnt1WhsLs%253D&amp;md5=998368b9130a020062a8c843e665ee82</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201502864"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rui, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Advanced Sodium-Ion Battery Composed of Carbon Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> in a Porous Graphene Network</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Advanced Sodium-Ion Battery Composed of Carbon Coated Na3V2(PO4)3 in a Porous Graphene Network</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rui, Xianhong; Sun, Wenping; Wu, Chao; Yu, Yan; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, to create efficient charge transfer, we propose a 3D hierarchical meso- and macroporous NVP-based hybrid cathode concept with connected Na ion/electron pathways for ultrafast charge and discharge NIBs, consisting of NVP nanocrystals coated with amorphous carbon and then wrapped by reduced graphene oxide nanosheets (abbreviated as NVP@C@rGO).  Specifically, i) the small nanograins shorten the lengths of solid-state Na ion diffusion, ii) the macro/mesopore network enables rapid ion transport and buffers the strain during repeated Na+ extn./insertion to maintain the structural integrity, iii) highly conductive amorphous coating carbon and rGO nanosheets facilitate fast electron transfer within the electrode and to the current collector.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biochemistry-derived porous carbon-encapsulated metal oxide nanocrystals for enhanced sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Yanping; Sun, Wenping; Rui, Xianhong; Zhou, Yan; Ng, Wun Jern; Yan, Qingyu; Fong, Eileen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">71-79</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transitional metal oxides are promising anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to their high theor. capacities and material abundance; however, their sodium storage capability is significantly hindered by the sluggish sodiation/desodiation reaction kinetics.  Herein, towards achieving fast and durable sodiation/desodiation reaction, Fe3O4 and Co3O4 nanocrystals encapsulated in carbon micro-spheres are synthesized via a biochem. approach using recombinant elastin-like polypeptides contg. hexahistidine tag (ELP16-His) followed by annealing.  Fe3O4 and Co3O4 nanocrystals of approx. 5 nm in size, which are uniformly dispersed in a carbon matrix, are obtained.  The carbon-encapsulated metal oxides exhibit encouraging sodium storage capacities (657 and 246 mA h g-1 at 0.1 and 2 A g-1, resp., for carbon-encapsulated Fe3O4; 583 and 183 mA h g-1 at 0.1 and 2 A g-1, resp., for carbon-encapsulated Co3O4), and have a high capacity retention after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g-1.  The superior electrochem. properties of the carbon-encapsulated metal oxide nanocrystals demonstrate their potential for use as anode materials for high-capacity, high-rate and durable sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr9gVqGB6AgdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh_O28Qwd46Jw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFOhu78%253D&amp;md5=f2a5002fac6e9e766ff7e780de975f4b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/nl500548a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Aken, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Maier, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon-Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Embedded in Porous Carbon Matrix: An Ultrafast Na-Storage Cathode with the Potential of Outperforming Li Cathodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">14</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2175</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2180</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Coated Na3V2(PO4)3 Embedded in Porous Carbon Matrix: An Ultrafast Na-Storage Cathode with the Potential of Outperforming Li Cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Song, Kepeng; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2175-2180</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries are one of the realistic promising alternatives to the Li analogs.  However, neither theor. energy/power d. nor the practical values reach the values of Li cathodes.  Poorer performance is expected owing to larger size, larger mass, and lower cell voltage.  Nonetheless, Na ion batteries are considered to be practically relevant in view of the abundance of the element Na.  The arguments in favor of Li and to the disadvantage of Na would be completely obsolete if the specific performance data of the latter would match the 1st.  Here the authors present a cathode consisting of C-coated nanosized Na3V2(PO4)3 embedded in a porous C matrix, which not only matches but even out-shines Li cathodes under high rate conditions.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cube-shaped Porous Carbon Derived from MOF-5 as Advanced Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Guoqiang; Jia, Xinnan; Huang, Zhaodong; Li, Simin; Liao, Hanxiao; Hou, Hongshuai; Huang, Lanping; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">196</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">413-421</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cube-shaped porous C (CPC) was obtained from the carbonization of MOF-5 (Zn4O(OOCC6H4COO)3) crystals and shows abundant micro/mesopores, high mech. strength, largest surface area (2316 m2 g-1, BET method) and good elec. cond. (a high wt. ratio 98.17/1.83 of C/O).  When used as anode material for Na-ion batteries, the CPC presents a high overall Na storage capacity ∼240 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles, and maintains a high specific capacity of 100 mAh g-1 after 5000 cycles at a c.d. of 3200 mA g-1.  For the advantages of this unique C framework structure, the CPC might be a promising anode material for the application of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4j83k5S9GX7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXgnrT0SlaZA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XktVClsbo%253D&amp;md5=3ed514e20ef47981e3ef939013c4f578</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b00942"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MnFe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub>@C Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">16</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3321</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3328</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b00942</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D3321-3328%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DC.%2BLiu%26author%3DN.%2BZhang%26author%3DM.%2BYu%26author%3DF.%2BJiao%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26title%3DMnFe2O4%2540C%2BNanofibers%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.6b00942&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11238&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b00942&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MnFe2O4@C Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Yu, Chuanming; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3321-3328</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnFe2O4 nanodots (∼3.3 nm) homogeneously dispersed in porous nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (denoted as MFO@C) were prepd. by a feasible electrospinning technique.  Meanwhile, MFO@C with the character of flexible free-standing membrane was directly used as binder- and current collector-free anode for sodium-ion batteries, exhibiting high electrochem. performance with high-rate capability (305 mA h g-1 at 10000 mA g-1 in comparison of 504 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1) and ultralong cycling life (ca. 90% capacity retention after 4200 cycles).  The Na-storage mechanism was systematically studied, revealing that MnFe2O4 is converted into metallic Mn and Fe after the first discharge (MnFe2O4 + 8Na+ + 8e- → Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O) and then to MnO and Fe2O3 during the following charge (Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O → MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e-).  The subsequent cycles occur through reversible redox reactions of MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e- &lt;-&gt; Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O, of which the redn./oxidn. of MnO/Mn takes place at a lower potential than that of Fe2O3/Fe.  Furthermore, a soft package sodium-ion full battery with MFO@C anode and Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C cathode was assembled, delivering a stable capacity of ∼400 mA h g-1 for MFO@C (with 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1) and a promising energy d. of 77.8 Wh kg-1 for the whole battery.  This is owing to the distinctive structure of very-fine MnFe2O4 nanodots embedded in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers, which effectively improves the utilization rate of active materials, facilitates the transportation of electrons and Na+ ions, and prevents the particle pulverization/agglomeration upon prolonged cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo_fovS2KMexbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXgnrT0SlaZA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XlsFKqtLk%253D&amp;md5=1f0fa2211d961158137c8cc4eb8fdd4c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2014.10.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospinning Preparation of Ultra-Long Aligned Nanofibers Thin Films for High Performance Fully Flexible Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">12</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">339</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">346</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospinning preparation of ultra-long aligned nanofibers thin films for high performance fully flexible lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Jian; Chen, Libao; Xu, Zhi; Lu, Bingan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) are of increasing interest as mobile power supply for the next-generation of flexible electronics.  The current flexible LIBs are generally limited by relatively poor ductility, short cycle-life and low charge and discharge rate.  Herein, we report a rational design and prepn. of flexible ultra-long, aligned carbon nanofibers thin films with embedded In2O3 nanocrystals (In2O3@FUACNFF) as a binder free anode for highly flexible LIBs.  In this work, needleless electrospinning has been demonstrated to be to an effective method for the prepn. of In2O3@FUACNFF with super-high throughput.  The In2O3@FUACNFF can ensure excellent charge transport, electrolyte transport and mech. flexibility, thus leading to excellent electrochem. performance and exceptional flexibility.  The In2O3@FUACNFF exhibited excellent cycling ability even after 500 cycles, with a capacity of 545.6 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 and rate performance even at the highest c.d. of 100 A g-1 with a reversible capacity of 224.2 mA h g-1.  Moreover, highly flexible full batteries were also fabricated to demonstrate the superior durability (the elec. stability of the manufd. flexible full battery was hardly affected after more than 120 times folding cycles), excellent cycle-ability (the capacity retention was almost 100% in the measured range from the 17th cycle on) and high rate performance (321.4 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 1000 mA g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_iwgeMmDlIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXgnrT0SlaZA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superhigh-Throughput Needleless Electrospinning Using a Rotary Cone as Spinneret</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Bingan; Wang, Yajiang; Liu, Yanxia; Duan, Huigao; Zhou, Jinyuan; Zhang, Zhenxing; Wang, Youqing; Li, Xiaodong; Wang, Wei; Lan, Wei; Xie, Erqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this communication, we report a needleless electrospinning setup using an electriferous rotating cone as the spinneret.  The typical prodn. rate by this method is about 10 g per min, which is 1000 times more than that of the traditional electrospinning method.  Nanofibers could be obtained as highly aligned arrays with lengths up to several centimeters by modifying the collector.  In addn., we found that it was the value of the voltage between the cone and the collector that affected the diam. of the electrospinning fibers.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun carbon nanofibers as anode materials for sodium ion batteries with excellent cycle performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Taiqiang; Liu, Yong; Pan, Likun; Lu, Ting; Yao, Yefeng; Sun, Zhuo; Chua, Daniel H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A simple and scalable electrospinning process followed by thermal treatment was used to fabricate carbon nanofibers.  The as-prepd. carbon nanofibers were investigated as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Remarkably, due to their weakly ordered turbostratic structure and a large interlayer spacing between graphene sheets, the carbon nanofibers exhibit a dominant adsorption/insertion sodium storage mechanism that shows high reversibility.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. performance of sodium-ion battery was improved by using functionalized interconnected N-doped carbon nanofibers (FN-CNFs) as the anode.  The material was synthesized with polypyrrole as precursor by a simple method.         </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped porous carbon sheets were successfully fabricated by chem. activation (KOH) of polypyrrole-functionalized graphene sheets.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of NiCoMnO4 nanoparticles as novel electrode materials for high-performance asymmetric energy storage devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pendashteh, Afshin; Palma, Jesus; Anderson, Marc; Marcilla, Rebeca</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
