            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In attempt to reduce the amt. of toxic Co in cobalt oxides, NiCoMnO4 nanoparticles were synthesized via a facile hydrothermal route and their electrochem. properties have been investigated as a novel electrode material for supercapacitors.  Samples have been characterized using X-ray diffraction (XRD), energy dispersive X-ray anal. (EDAX), and XPS.  N2 adsorption/desorption measurements demonstrated a high sp. surface area of 175 m2 g-1.  The morphol. of the samples has been probed with scanning (SEM) and transmission (TEM) electron microscopy.  The electrochem. properties of the NiCoMnO4 nanoparticles have been evaluated as electrode materials for energy storage application by means of various electrochem. techniques including cyclic voltammetry, galvanostatic charge-discharge measurements, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  According to the obtained results, the NiCoMnO4 electrodes showed significant improved capacitive performance in comparison with pure oxides (e.g. NiO, Co3O4, and Mn3O4).  The NiCoMnO4 electrodes with a high mass loading of ∼10 mg cm-2 exhibited a high specific capacitance of 510 F g-1 at 1 A g-1, and a desirable rate capability (retaining 285 F g-1 at 10 A g-1).  Finally, asym. devices based on NiCoMnO4 nanoparticles as pos. electrodes and reduced graphene oxide nanosheets as neg. electrodes were assembled, showing a remarkable performance including high energy (20 W h kg-1), and stunning power d.(37.5 kW kg-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYIuamQcCPRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh565CnJswEkA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XktVOqtLo%253D&amp;md5=9a0a6142a7c63863868fe99240a567e1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b11022"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Novel and Facile One-Pot Solvothermal Synthesis of PEDOT-PSS/Ni-Mn-Co-O Hybrid as an Advanced Supercapacitor Electrode Material</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Novel and Facile One-Pot Solvothermal Synthesis of PEDOT-PSS/Ni-Mn-Co-O Hybrid as an Advanced Supercapacitor Electrode Material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Chengjie; Yang, Chunming; Jiang, Min; Deng, Cuifen; Yang, Lishan; Li, Junhua; Qian, Dong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, a novel and facile one-pot method has been developed for the synthesis of a hybrid consisting of Ni-Mn-Co ternary oxide and poly(3,4-ethylenedioxythiophene)-polystyrenesulfonate (PEDOT-PSS/NMCO) with a hierarchical three-dimensional net structure via a solvothermal-copptn. coupled with oxidative polymn. route.  Apart from the achievement of polymn., copptn., and solvothermal in one pot, the hydroxyl (OH-) ions generated from the oxidative polymn. of org. monomer by neutral KMnO4 soln. were skillfully employed as precipitants for metal ions.  As compared with the PEDOT-PSS/Ni-Mn binary oxide, PEDOT-PSS/Co-Mn binary oxide, and PEDOT-PSS/MnO2, PEDOT-PSS1.5/NMCO exhibits overwhelmingly superior supercapacitive performance, more specifically, a high specific capacitance of 1234.5 F g-1 at a c.d. of 1 A g-1, a good capacitance retention of 83.7% at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1 after 1000 cycles, an energy d. of 51.9 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 275 W kg-1, and an energy d. of 21.4 W h kg-1 at an extremely elevated power d. of 5500 W kg-1.  Noticeably, the energy d. and power d. of PEDOT-PSS/NMCO are by far higher than those of the existing analogs recently reported.  The exceptional performance of PEDOT-PSS/NMCO benefits from its unique mesoporous architecture, which could provide a larger reaction surface area, faster ion and electron transfer ability, and good structural stability.  The desirable integrated performance enables the multicomponent composite to be a promising electrode material for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGozvXm1oiYEXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh565CnJswEkA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XltlKgsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=9c184e9e4118be7a915933878bbcd727</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1021/am5048653"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tu, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Spinel Manganese-Nickel-Cobalt Ternary Oxide Nanowire Array for High-Performance Electrochemical Capacitor Applications</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A membraneless alkaline direct liquid fuel cell (DLFC) platform developed with a catalyst-selective strategy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Xingwen; Pascual, Emilio J.; Wauson, Joshua C.; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">With a logical management of the catalyst selectivity, we present a scalable, membraneless alk. direct liq. fuel cell (DLFC) platform.  The uniqueness of this innovation is that the inexpensive (non-platinum) cathode catalysts, based on strongly coupled transition-metal-oxide nanocrystals and nano-structured carbon materials (e. g., NiCo2O4 nano-particles on a nitrogen-doped graphene and MnNiCoO4 nano-particles on a nitrogen-doped multi-wall carbon nanotube), exhibit high activity for the oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) but without activity for the anode fuel oxidn. reaction (FOR).  Therefore, operation of the DLFCs allows the anode fuel to freely enter the cathode.  This strategy avoids the reliance on expensive or difficult-to-develop cation- or anion-exchange membranes and circumvents the scalability concerns of the conventional membraneless DLFCs that are operated under a laminar-flow principle.  With proper catalyst selectivity, a variety of org. liqs. can be used as anode fuels.  The high power d. delivered by the membraneless DLFCs with inexpensive components and safe fuels can enable the development of not only small-scale portable power sources but also large-scale energy generation systems for transportation and stationary storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqfBV1_WylSKrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljxqTZiAZor-A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFaqsb7K&amp;md5=c937172a6dd7f7d8ec699d60438942b8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, J.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of Sr-doping on the electrical properties of MnCoNiO4 NTC ceramics</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Junhua; Yao, Jincheng; Chen, Zhaoyang; Fan, Yanwei; Chang, Aimin; Jia, Dianzeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science: Materials in Electronics</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The effects of Sr-doping on Ni-Mn-Co-O spinel-structured NTC ceramics were investigated.  And the precursors of Sr-doped NiCoMnO4 NTC ceramics were attained by solid state reactions at room temp., with no intermediate compds.  Its formation and the structural evolutions were characterized by thermo-gravimetry-differential scanning calorimetry, X-ray diffraction and SEM with energy dispersive spectroscopy.  Related elec. analyses were also performed.  The values of R298K, B298/323 const. and the temp. coeff. of resistance α298K of the thermistors are in the range of 168-1,738 Ω, 3,257-3,359 K and -3.64 to -3.78 % K-1, resp.  Complex impedance anal. shows, for x = 0.2, single semicircular arc whose shape does not have any change with temp.  The grain boundary properties exhibit thermistor parameters with a neg. temp. coeff. characteristic.  The conduction for the grain boundary could be explained by oxygen vacancies.  The results show that the ceramics exhibits a good elec. property because of narrow grain size distribution, controlled morphol., and high purity.  This suggests that the elec. properties can be adjusted to desired values by controlling the Sr cation content.  This series of materials could be considered as practical materials for NTC thermistor.  Most importantly, this new approach greatly simplifies the prepn. processes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqTsvOTmCeno7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljxqTZiAZor-A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVyju78%253D&amp;md5=9e485c8619aad6fb36e15edd9afec7ca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.materresbull.2015.03.065"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lei, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layer-by-Layer Assembly of Manganese-Cobalt-Nickel Oxide Nanosheets/Graphene Composite Films</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Mater.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layer-by-layer assembly of manganese-cobalt-nickel oxide nanosheets/graphene composite films</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Mingze; Kang, Liping; Liu, Chunling; Lei, Zhibing; Liu, Zong-Huai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Research Bulletin</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">68</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two different nanosheets, poly(diallyldimethylammonium chloride)-functionalized graphene nanosheets (FRGO) and manganese-cobalt-nickel oxide nanosheets (MnCoNiO2) are used as building blocks for the assembly of manganese-cobalt-nickel oxide nanosheets/graphene composite films (MnCoNiO2-FRGO).  Sequential adsorption of these oppositely-charged nanosheets yields multilayer films, whereas simple mixing produces a lamellar flocculate.  UV-visible spectra exhibit a progressive increase of absorbance with increasing no. of deposition cycles, providing strong evidence for the regular growth of multilayer films.  The combination of FRGO and MnCoNiO2 nanosheets produces a new layered structure with a planar spacing of 2.36 nm, which is in agreement with the sum of the thicknesses of MnCoNiO2 and FRGO nanosheets.  The MnCoNiO2-FRGO composite films show a higher specific capacitance and good electrochem. stability because of a synergistic effect existed between the FRGO nanosheets and MnCoNiO2 nanosheets.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdqVJArYyMprVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljpR-tPNyDPNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXlsV2nsbg%253D&amp;md5=064a004b7f44fd836ca12519e903ab4a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b04280"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qi, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiCoMnO<sub>4</sub>: A Bifunctional Affinity Probe for His-Tagged Protein Purification and Phosphorylation Sites Recognition</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and characterization of Mn-Co-Ni-O ceramic nanoparticles by reverse microemulsion method</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Long; Kong, Wenwen; Yao, Jincheng; Zhang, Huimin; Gao, Bo; Li, Yonglei; Bu, Haijun; Chang, Aimin; Jiang, Chunping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ceramics International</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mn-Co-Ni-O ultrafine ceramic nanoparticles are successfully synthesized by the reverse microemulsion method in a triton X-100/n-hexanol/cyclohexane system.  The thermal decompn. process, crystallinity and crystal structure of Mn-Co-Ni-O powders are investigated and characterized by thermogravimetric-differential scanning calorimetry (TG/DSC), Fourier Transform IR (FT-IR), X-ray powders diffraction (XRD) and High Resoln. Transmission Electron Microscope (HRTEM), resp.  The TGA/DSC, FT-IR and XRD results show that the reverse microemulsion method can effectively reduce the calcination temp. to 600°C for synthesizing cubic spinel phase Mn-Co-Ni-O ceramic particles.  Furthermore, the XRD and HRTEM images reveal that the particles are highly cryst. and have a narrow and uniform particle size distribution.  These findings indicate that Mn-Co-Ni-O nanoparticles prepd. via reverse microemulsion process meet demands for obtaining better microstructure and performance of Mn-Co-Ni-O materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdZc72sek31bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljpR-tPNyDPNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVemt7fF&amp;md5=ee25a3224cddbe705f20073ff7d649b8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1038/nmat4170"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Raccichini, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Varzi, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Passerini, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Scrosati, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Role of Graphene for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of metal oxide/reduced graphene oxide hybrids with high lithium storage capacity and stable cyclability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Jixin; Zhu, Ting; Zhou, Xiaozhu; Zhang, Yanyan; Lou, Xiong Wen; Chen, Xiaodong; Zhang, Hua; Hng, Huey Hoon; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1084-1089</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report an environment-friendly approach to synthesize transition metal oxide nanoparticles (NPs)/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) sheets hybrids by combining the redn. of graphene oxide (GO) with the growth of metal oxide NPs in one step.  Either Fe2O3 or CoO NPs were grown onto rGO sheets in EtOH soln. through a solvothermal process, during which GOs were reduced to rGO without the addn. of any strong reducing agent, e.g. hydrazine, or requiring any post-high-temp. annealing process.  The GO or rGO during the pptn. of metal oxide NPs may act as heterogeneous nucleation seeds to facilitate the formation of small crystal grains.  This may allow more efficient diffusion of Li ions and lead to high specific capacities.  These metal oxide NPs-rGO hybrids were used as anodes for Li-ion batteries, which showed high capacities and excellent charge-discharge cycling stability in the voltage window between 0.01 and 3.0 V.  For example, Fe2O3 NPs/rGO hybrids showed specific capacity of 881 mA h g-1 in the 90th cycle at a discharge c.d. of 302 mA g-1 (0.3 C), while CoO NPs/rGO hybrids showed a lower capacity of 600 mA h g-1 in the 90th cycle at a discharge c.d. of 215 mA g-1 (0.3 C).  These nanohybrids also show excellent capacities at high C rate currents, e.g. 611 mA h g-1 for Fe2O3/rGO sample in the 300th cycle at 2014 mA g-1 (2 C).  Such synthesis technique can be a promising route to produce advanced electrode materials for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXP25LIQ9WI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljpR-tPNyDPNw"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1039/c2nr33576j</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D2045-2054%26journal%3DNanoscale%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BXiong%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26title%3DA%2BFacile%2BRoute%2Bto%2BSynthesize%2BMultiporous%2BMnCo2O4%2Band%2BCoMn2O4%2BSpinel%2BQuasi-Hollow%2BSpheres%2Bwith%2BImproved%2BLithium%2BStorage%2BProperties%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc2nr33576j&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11238&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc2nr33576j&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A facile route to synthesize multiporous MnCo2O4 and CoMn2O4 spinel quasi-hollow spheres with improved lithium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jingfa; Xiong, Shenglin; Li, Xiaowei; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2045-2054</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile and general way for the synthesis of porous and hollow complex oxides is highly desirable owing to their significant applications for energy storage and other fields.  In this contribution, uniform Mn0.33Co0.67CO3 and Co0.33Mn0.67CO3 microspheres are firstly fabricated solvothermally just by tuning the molar ratio of Mn and Co.  Subsequently, the growth of multiporous MnCo2O4 and CoMn2O4 quasi-hollow microspheres by topotactic chem. transformation from the corresponding precursors are realized through a non-equil. heat treatment process.  Topotactic conversion further demonstrated that the much larger CoMn2O4 pores than those of MnCo2O4 are possibly due to the longer transfer distance of ions.  When evaluated as anode materials for LIBs (lithium ion batteries), after 25 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1, the resultant MnCo2O4 and CoMn2O4 quasi-hollow microspheres possessed reversible capacities of 755 and 706 mA h g-1, resp.  In particular, the MnCo2O4 samples could deliver a reversible capacity as high as 610 mA h g-1 even at a higher c.d. of 400 mA g-1 with excellent electrochem. stability after 100 cycles of testing, indicating its potential application in LIBs.  We believe that such good performance results from the appropriate pore size and quasi-hollow nature of MnCo2O4 microspheres, which can effectively buffer the large vol. variation of anodes based on the conversion reaction during Li+ insertion/extn.  The present strategy is simple but very effective, and due to its versatility, it can be extended to other binary, even ternary complex metal oxides with high-performance in LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrbhvspDIEXS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljht3WLCS7BWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXis1Chtb0%253D&amp;md5=6077ea996d47a6809543d23637a09546</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.01.105"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qin, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Microspheres Derived from Oatmeal as High Capacity and Superior Long Life Anode Material for Sodium Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped carbon microspheres derived from oatmeal as high capacity and superior long life anode material for sodium ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Dong; Yu, Caiyan; Zhang, Xiaojie; Qin, Wei; Lu, Ting; Hu, Bingwen; Li, Huili; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">191</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped C microspheres (NCSs) derived from oatmeal are employed as anodes for Na ion batteries (SIBs).  Their morphol., structure and electrochem. performance were characterized by field emission SEM, x-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, XPS, N adsorption-desorption isotherms, galvanostatic charge/discharge tests, cyclic voltammetry and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, resp.  NCSs treated at 500° exhibit a high max. charge capacity of 336 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 and even at a high c.d. of 10 A g-1 within 70 s charging time, a capacity of 104 mA h g-1 is maintained after 12500 cycles without obvious decay.  The high capacity, excellent rate performance, long life cycling and ultrafast rechargeable ability enable the NCSs to be a promising candidate for practical SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoMLNKZGaDv-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljht3WLCS7BWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtlWjtbc%253D&amp;md5=27ba87f782244e7692481a3e78d2d55d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref59'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE00941G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultra-Thick Graphene Bulk Supercapacitor Electrodes for Compact Energy Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-thick graphene bulk supercapacitor electrodes for compact energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Huan; Tao, Ying; Zheng, Xiaoyu; Luo, Jiayan; Kang, Feiyu; Cheng, Hui-Ming; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3135-3142</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Compact energy storage with high volumetric performance is highly important.  However, the state-of-the-art electrodes and devices remain far from the requirements due to the lack of consideration from a device perspective, which not only demands a high specific gravimetric capacity, but also needs to take into account operation voltage, material d. and electrode thickness.  We develop a novel approach to fabricate a monolithic ultra-thick and dense carbon electrode for sym. supercapacitors, starting with graphene assembly and taking all the above factors into consideration.  We found that zinc chloride is an ideal sacrificial pore former, and taken together with capillary drying can tune the sp. surface area of the monolithic graphene from 370 to over 1000 m2 g-1 while the monoliths maintain a high d. from 1.6 to 0.6 g cm-3.  Having a good balance of porosity and d., the directly sliced graphene pellet electrode with a thickness up to 400 μm delivers a capacitance of 150 F cm-3 in an ionic liq. electrolyte, corresponding to a volumetric energy d. of ∼65 W h L-1 for a sym. supercapacitor device, the highest value reported to date for supercapacitors.  This study presents a design principle for electrode materials towards next-generation energy storage devices, not limited to supercapacitors, which are becoming smaller, lighter but more energetic.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoAQiQ3Is7rb7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljht3WLCS7BWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XotF2qtrs%253D&amp;md5=b1d91a6572e5f1cc75a750fea90da967</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref60'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Augustyn, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Come, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lowe, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tolbert, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Abruña, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Simon, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dunn, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Rate Electrochemical Energy Storage through LiC Intercalation Pseudocapacitance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">518-522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljht3WLCS7BWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref61'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1021/jp074464w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Polleux, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lim, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dunn, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO<sub>2</sub> (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages of using nanostructured materials for electrochem. energy storage have focused on the benefits assocd. with short path lengths.  However, another contribution, capacitive effects which become increasingly important at nanoscale dimensions, was studied.  Nanocryst. TiO2 (anatase) was studied over a dimensional regime where both capacitive and Li intercalation processes contribute to the total stored charge.  An anal. of the voltammetric sweep data was used to distinguish between the amt. of charge stored by these 2 processes.  At particle sizes &lt;10 nm, capacitive contributions became increasingly important, leading to greater amts. of total stored charge (gravimetrically normalized) with decreasing TiO2 particle size.  The area normalized capacitance is well &gt;100 μF/cm2, confirming that the capacitive contribution was pseudocapacitive.  Also, decreasing the particle size to the nanoscale regime led to faster charge/discharge rates because diffusion-controlled Li ion intercalation was replaced by faradaic reactions which occur at the surface of the material.  The charge storage and kinetic benefits derived from using nanoscale metal oxides provide an interesting direction for the design of materials that offer both power d. and energy d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0ueeFhvSDZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZ87BaUxu6WQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXhtVChs7zL&amp;md5=b47809cb86f6cf28f5758e0eb3eac71e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref62'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit62" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201404472"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lin, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fast and Large Lithium Storage in 3D Porous VN Nanowires-Graphene Composite as a Superior Anode toward High-Performance Hybrid Supercapacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Funct. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">25</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2270</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2278</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201404472</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D25%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D2270-2278%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26author%3DT.%2BWang%26author%3DW.%2BLang%26author%3DP.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BLin%26author%3DB.%2BYan%26title%3DFast%2Band%2BLarge%2BLithium%2BStorage%2Bin%2B3D%2BPorous%2BVN%2BNanowires-Graphene%2BComposite%2Bas%2Ba%2BSuperior%2BAnode%2Btoward%2BHigh-Performance%2BHybrid%2BSupercapacitors%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201404472&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11238&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201404472&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fast and Large Lithium Storage in 3D Porous VN Nanowires-Graphene Composite as a Superior Anode Toward High-Performance Hybrid Supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Rutao; Lang, Junwei; Zhang, Peng; Lin, Zongyuan; Yan, Xingbin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2270-2278</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-ion hybrid capacitors (LIHCs), consisting of an energy-type redox anode and a power-type double-layer cathode, are attracting significant attention due to the good combination with the advantages of conventional Li-ion batteries and supercapacitors.  However, most anodes are battery-like materials with the sluggish kinetics of Li-ion storage, which seriously restrict the energy storage of LIHCs at the high charge/discharge rates.  Herein, vanadium nitride (VN) nanowire is demonstrated to have obvious pseudocapacitive characteristic of Li-ion storage and can get further gains in energy storage through a 3D porous architecture with the assistance of conductive reduced graphene oxide (RGO).  The as-prepd. 3D VN-RGO composite exhibits the large Li-ion storage capacity and fast charge/discharge rate within a wide working widow from 0.01-3 V (vs. Li/Li+), which could potentially boost the operating potential and the energy and power densities of LIHCs.  By employing such 3D VN-RGO composite and porous carbon nanorods with a high surface area of 3343 m2 g-1 as the anode and cathode, resp., a novel LIHCs is fabricated with an ultrahigh energy d. of 162 Wh kg-1 at 200 W kg-1, which also remains 64 Wh kg-1 even at a high power d. of 10 kW kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoVXl_sHI4udrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZ87BaUxu6WQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvF2gtLY%253D&amp;md5=cb9a635333a988e76063378327023ab7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref63'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit63" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2003.10.016"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jow, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Impedance Study on the Low Temperature of Li-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2004</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">49</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1057</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1061</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2003.10.016</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D49%26publication_year%3D2004%26pages%3D1057-1061%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DS.%2BZhang%26author%3DK.%2BXu%26author%3DR.%2BJow%26title%3DElectrochemical%2BImpedance%2BStudy%2Bon%2Bthe%2BLow%2BTemperature%2Bof%2BLi-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2003.10.016&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11238&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2003.10.016&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical impedance study on the low temperature of Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, S. S.; Xu, K.; Jow, T. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2004</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1057-1061</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cycling performance of Li-ion batteries was studied by using electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  Results showed that total resistance of the Li-ion batteries is mainly composed of bulk resistance (Rb), solid-state interface resistance (Rsei) and charge-transfer resistance (Rct).  During cycling, the Rb and Rsei do not change while the Rct displays two min. in the same voltage regions where the major peaks of differential capacities are present.  The Rct can be linked to kinetics of the battery electrochem. reaction.  In response to the temp. change, the Rb and Rsei vary in a very similar manner, while the Rct shows significant difference.  In the fully charged and discharged states as well as at the low temps. (≤20°), the total resistance of the Li-ion batteries is predominated by the Rct.  Using the term of the Rct, we explained two low-temp. phenomena of the Li-ion battery: (a) charging of a fully discharged battery is much more difficult than discharging of a fully charged battery, and (b) both the power (operating voltage) and energy (delivered capacity) are substantially reduced.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplYUwg57Nby7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZ87BaUxu6WQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2cXmtFWmsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=1be699464091e1d4ed024d22eb3540bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref64'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2011.02.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Manivannan, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cyclability Study of Silicon-Carbon Composite Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries Using Electrochemical Impedance Spectroscopy</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">56</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3981</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3987</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2011.02.014</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D56%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D3981-3987%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DJ.%2BGuo%26author%3DA.%2BSun%26author%3DX.%2BChen%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26author%3DA.%2BManivannan%26title%3DCyclability%2BStudy%2Bof%2BSilicon-Carbon%2BComposite%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%2BUsing%2BElectrochemical%2BImpedance%2BSpectroscopy%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2011.02.014&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b11238&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2011.02.014&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit64R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">64</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cyclability study of silicon-carbon composite anodes for lithium-ion batteries using electrochemical impedance spectroscopy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Juchen; Sun, Ann; Chen, Xilin; Wang, Chunsheng; Manivannan, Ayyakkannu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">56</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3981-3987</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The effects of carbonization process and C nanofiber/nanotube additives on the cycling stability of Si-C composite anodes were studied by monitoring the impedance evolution during charge/discharge cycles with electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS).  Three types of Si-C anodes were studied: the 1st type consisted of Si nanoparticles incorporated into a network of C nanofibers (CNFs) and multi-walled C nanotubes (MWNTs), with annealed polymer binder.  The 2nd type of Si-C anodes was prepd. by further heat treatment of the 1st Si-C anodes to carbonize the polymer binder.  The 3rd Si-C anode was as same as the 2nd one except no CNFs and MWNTs being added.  Impedance anal. revealed that the carbonization process stabilized the Si-C anode structure and decreased the charge transfer resistance, thus improving the cycling stability.  However, although the MWNTs/CNFs additives could enhance the electronic cond. of the Si-C anodes, the induced inhomogeneous structure decreased the integrity of the electrode, resulting in a poor long term cycling stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8R3BLiB75k7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljULCmQCrKHJA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXkslCnsbk%253D&amp;md5=8a1f09ef0a807a6aed6d3e345e2814f2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref65"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref65'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">65</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit65" data-doi="10.1002/9780470381588"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Orazem, M.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, to create efficient charge transfer, we propose a 3D hierarchical meso- and macroporous NVP-based hybrid cathode concept with connected Na ion/electron pathways for ultrafast charge and discharge NIBs, consisting of NVP nanocrystals coated with amorphous carbon and then wrapped by reduced graphene oxide nanosheets (abbreviated as NVP@C@rGO).  Specifically, i) the small nanograins shorten the lengths of solid-state Na ion diffusion, ii) the macro/mesopore network enables rapid ion transport and buffers the strain during repeated Na+ extn./insertion to maintain the structural integrity, iii) highly conductive amorphous coating carbon and rGO nanosheets facilitate fast electron transfer within the electrode and to the current collector.  The designed NVP@C@rGO cathode is shown to achieve excellent rate capability (86 mA h/g at 100 C) and outstandingcycling stability (64% retention after 10000 cycles at 100 C), indicating its superiority in practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsi-wIi2kQlbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgjId3pxpSpwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsF2ksrrM&amp;md5=7861bc14c4a3396b8223e56a8e698e3b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee40811f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hong, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Charge Carriers in Rechargeable Batteries: Na Ions vs. Li Ions</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Charge carriers in rechargeable batteries: Na ions vs. Li ions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Sung You; Kim, Youngjin; Park, Yuwon; Choi, Aram; Choi, Nam-Soon; Lee, Kyu Tae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  We discuss the similarities and dissimilarities of sodium- and lithium-ion batteries in terms of neg. and pos. electrodes.  Compared to the comprehensive body of work on lithium-ion batteries, research on sodium-ion batteries is still at the germination stage.  Since both sodium and lithium are alkali metals, they share similar chem. properties including ionicity, electronegativity and electrochem. reactivity.  They accordingly have comparable synthetic protocols and electrochem. performances, which indicates that sodium-ion batteries can be successfully developed based on previously applied approaches or methods in the lithium counterpart.  The electrode materials in Li-ion batteries provide the best library for research on Na-ion batteries because many Na-ion insertion hosts have their roots in Li-ion insertion hosts.  However, the larger size and different bonding characteristics of sodium ions influence the thermodn. and/or kinetic properties of sodium-ion batteries, which leads to unexpected behavior in electrochem. performance and reaction mechanism, compared to lithium-ion batteries.  This perspective provides a comparative overview of the major developments in the area of pos. and neg. electrode materials in both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries in the past decade.  Highlighted are concepts in solid state chem. and electrochem. that have provided new opportunities for tailored design that can be extended to many different electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHBS0wIkomorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgjId3pxpSpwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWmtL%252FE&amp;md5=023136cc0e5ed94e18ce0d526a0000a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1038/nnano.2015.194"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pasta, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorene-Graphene Hybrid Material as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                 10.1038/nnano.2015.194</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-985</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1748-3387</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAucZXUrxyyQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201404549"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Ultrastable Anode for Long-Life Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are important alternative energy storage devices that have recently come again into focus for the development of large-scale energy storage devices because sodium is an abundant and low-cost material.  However, the development of electrode materials with long-term stability has remained a great challenge.  A novel anode material, a P2-type layered oxide with the chem. compn. Na2/3Co1/3Ti2/3O2, exhibits outstanding cycle stability (∼84.84% capacity retention after 3000 cycles, very small decrease in the vol. (0.046%) after 500 cycles), good rate capability (∼41% capacity retention at a discharge/charge rate of 10C), and a usable reversible capacity of ∼90 mA-h/g with a safe av. storage voltage of ∼0.7 V in the sodium half-cell.  This P2-type layered oxide is a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries with a long cycle life and should greatly promote the development of room-temp. sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-JAcvjHnFdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAucZXUrxyyQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVamurnO&amp;md5=201a1be3b549c0ff238f63889e25b7a3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201500919"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ahmed, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Anjum, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hedhili, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alshareef, N.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mechanistic Insight into the Stability of HfO<sub>2</sub>-Coated MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheet Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Small</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">11</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4341</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4350</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is demonstrated for the first time that surface passivation of 2D nanosheets of MoS2 by an ultrathin and uniform layer of HfO2 can significantly improve the cyclic performance of sodium ion batteries.  After 50 charge/discharge cycles, bare MoS2 and HfO2 coated MoS2 electrodes deliver the specific capacity of 435 and 636 mAh g-1, resp., at c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  These results imply that batteries using HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes retain 91% of the initial capacity; in contrast, bare MoS2 anodes retain only 63%.  Also, HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes show one of the highest reported capacity values for MoS2.  Cyclic voltammetry and XPS results suggest that HfO2 does not take part in electrochem. reaction.  The mechanism of capacity retention with HfO2 coating is explained by ex situ transmission electron microscope imaging and elec. impedance spectroscopy.  HfO2 acts as a passivation layer at the anode/electrolyte interface and prevents structural degrdn. during charge/discharge process.  Moreover, the amorphous nature of HfO2 allows facile diffusion of Na ions.  These results clearly show the potential of HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes, which performance is significantly higher than previous reports where bulk MoS2 or composites of MoS2 with carbonaceous materials are used.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqG15e3D2W7WLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAucZXUrxyyQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXpvVegsbo%253D&amp;md5=2b2108aa242063c6214974eaf43cfbb4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1149/1.1393348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stevens, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahn, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity Anode Materials for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have attracted extensive interest for energy storage and conversion as an alternative to lithium-ion batteries.  The development of advanced electrode materials is important for the implementation of sodium-ion batteries into practical applications.  Herein, we developed a facile soaking-chem. vapor deposition method to grow core-sheath structured Sn@CNT nanopillar arrays on carbon paper with a unique 3D hierarchical architecture as free-standing electrode for sodium-ion batteries.  The electrode achieved a reversible capacity of 887 μA h cm-2 in the first cycle and good cyclability extending to 100 cycles.  The electrode also demonstrated a promising rate capability, which is suitable for high power applications. The full sodium-ion battery can power LED lights.  This work is expected to inspire the development of sustainable sodium-ion batteries for energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGozaFfJuwFGzLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAucZXUrxyyQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjsFGnt7g%253D&amp;md5=5c384dc0e6aaf8343724bf03c0f442f7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1021/nn503582c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS<sub>2</sub> to Orthorhombic-SnS</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8323</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8333</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS2 to Orthorhombic-SnS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Tengfei; Pang, Wei Kong; Zhang, Chaofeng; Yang, Jianping; Chen, Zhixin; Liu, Hua Kun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWHE3xEPCjvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAucZXUrxyyQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Non-lithium metals such as Na have attracted attention as a potential charge carrying ion for rechargeable batteries.  Using in situ TEM in combination with d. functional theory calcns., the authors probed the structural and chem. evolution of SnO2 nanowire anodes in Na-ion batteries and compared them quant. with results from Li-ion batteries.  Upon Na insertion into SnO2, a displacement reaction occurs, giving amorphous NaxSn nanoparticles dispersed in Na2O matrix.  With further Na insertion, the NaxSn crystd. into Na15Sn4 (x = 3.75).  Upon extn. of Na (de-sodiation), the NaxSn transforms to Sn nanoparticles.  Assocd. with the de-alloying, pores form, leading to a structure of Sn particles confined in a hollow matrix of Na2O.  These pores greatly increase elec. impedance, therefore accounting for the poor cyclability of SnO2.  DFT calcns. indicate that Na+ diffuses 30 times slower than Li+ in SnO2, in agreement with in situ TEM measurement.  Insertion of Na can chemomechanically soften the reaction product to a greater extent than in lithiation.  Therefore, in contrast to the lithiation of SnO2 significantly less dislocation plasticity was seen ahead of the sodiation front.  This direct comparison of the results from Na and Li highlights the crit. role of ionic size and electronic structure of different ionic species on the charge/discharge rate and failure mechanisms in these batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxbnVD4FT9W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljqteDGNqzVlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFels7zP&amp;md5=3eeb24d9885b1c825918e689b7adbbb2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201305638"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Woo, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mok, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ryu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oh, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Phosphide as a Promising Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the abundance and low cost of sodium-contg. precursors ambient temp. sodium ion batteries are promising for large scale grid storage.  The low m.p. of Na (97.7 °C) compared to 180.6 °C for Li represents a significant safety hazard for the use of Na metal anodes at ambient temps., which emphasizes the need for scientists and engineers to identify, design and develop new neg. electrodes for Na-ion batteries.  The identification of a suitable neg. electrode is a crucial challenge for any further successful development of new cells, and to date efficient and competitive neg. electrodes for NaB are still very rare.  In this work we demonstrate that NiP3 could be a good challenger for this purpose.  NiP3 based electrodes are evaluated as neg. electrode materials for Li-ion batteries (LiB) and Na-ion batteries (NaB).  The study of the reaction mechanism reveals the formation of a phase of compn. close to Li3P and Na3P embedding Ni nanoparticles as the final reaction product after a full discharge.  While the direct conversion of NiP3 into Na3P is identified for the reaction vs. Na, it is still unclear whether an amorphous phase exists during the first discharge for the reaction vs. Li before the conversion.  Furthermore, thanks to the CM-cellulose/carbon black (CMC/CB) electrode formulation, the NiP3 electrode possesses a very promising capacity with a reversible storage capacity higher than 1000 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles for LiB and 900 mA h g-1 after 15 cycles for NaB, which represents one of the highest capacities ever sustained in Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOUBqz1xXoSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljqteDGNqzVlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpslGjug%253D%253D&amp;md5=1e5512e9a0282ca35cdf95497825a466</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA09867J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ye, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Iron-Based Sodium-Ion Full Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.
