        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries have been an active area of research over the past several years.  While a great deal of attention is now focused on the development and evaluation of single electrode materials, much less is paid to their combined performance in full batteries.  Most full batteries currently available suffer from rapid capacity fading under extended cycling.  In this study, we prep. ultra-small, poorly cryst. FeOx nanoparticles supported on carbon nanotubes as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It exhibits excellent half-cell performances; and, when combined with a Prussian blue cathode material, it leads to iron-based full batteries.  Our prototypes have a working voltage of ∼2 V, specific energy d. of ∼136 W h kg-1 and, most impressively, outstanding cycling stability at both low and high current rates with negligible capacity loss.  Owing to their low material and fabrication cost, long cycle life and high efficiency, we believe that these iron-based sodium-ion batteries would be highly appealing toward the stationary energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGolrxMNOb7GMrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljqteDGNqzVlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitVyqsbzF&amp;md5=317f81b31e1e8d8b0c5f729fd16dbc57</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1021/cm025556v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alcántara, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jaraba, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lavela, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tirado, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiCo<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Spinel: First Report on a Transition Metal Oxide for the Negative Electrode of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Micelle-templated ordered mesoporous nickel-cobalt carbonates and oxides are fabricated using a metal nitrate-citric acid strategy, which avoids the hydrolysis and aging requirements assocd. with sol-gel chem.  A series of mesoporous NixCo(3-x)(CO3)y and NixCo(3-x)O4 films with varying Ni-Co compns. and 14 ± 4 nm mesopores are fabricated with the same block copolymer template.  AFM and GISAXS anal. indicates that the mesostructure is maintained through the formation of the carbonate and oxide, while GIXD profiles confirm formation of pure spinel phases of semi-cryst. NixCo(3-x)O4.  The micelle templated mesopores are interconnected and provide transport paths for the electrolyte to minimize the solid-state diffusion requirements assocd. with battery electrodes.  These materials exhibit good performance as sodium ion battery anodes even at high current densities of 4 A g-1.  Amongst the mixed-metal oxides, Ni2CoO4 exhibits the highest specific capacity of 239 mA h g-1 after galvanostatic cycling at a c.d. of 1 A g-1 for 10 cycles.  The superior performance of Ni2CoO4 at high rates is attributed to the high surface area and short ion-diffusion paths of the nanoporous anode architecture, while the higher nickel content in the mixed metal oxide provides enhanced stability during oxide formation along with enhanced electronic cond., leading to improved cycling stability of the anode.  This micelle template metal nitrate-citric acid method enables new possibilities for fabricating variety of ordered mesoporous mixed-metal carbonates and oxides that could be used in a wide range of applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOj35oA0taBbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljqteDGNqzVlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFWhtLzJ&amp;md5=18622fb821b1321e7d25704a26915e57</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1038/nmat1368"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Arico, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bruce, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Scrosati, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Schalkwijk, W.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructured Materials for Advanced Energy Conversion and Storage Devices</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Outstanding Na and Li storage capability is successfully demonstrated in ultrathin NiO nanosheets (4-5 nm in thickness) synthesized via a facile solvothermal process followed by annealing in air.  For Na storage, the NiO nanosheets deliver a high reversible specific capacity of 299 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 1 A g-1, and the capacity still remains up to 154 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1.  Upon charge/discharge cycling, the specific capacity maintains to be ≤266 mA h g-1 during the 100th cycle at 1 A g-1.  Such Na storage capability of NiO nanosheets is by far one of the best reported for transition metal oxides.  For Li storage, the cell achieves a high reversible specific capacity of 1242 and 250 mA h g-1 at 0.2 and 15 A g-1, resp.  The capacity for Li storage maintains to be 851 mA h g-1 during the 170th cycle at 2 A g-1.  Ultrathin NiO nanosheets are highly attractive for fast Na/Li diffusion with high-rate capability for rechargeable Na-ion batteries (SIBs) and Li-ion batteries (LIBs).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-6AFm_88BSLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhH-acJgo8vdg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVamtr3I&amp;md5=245647026fd3b90db2f4ffdae97cb290</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1038/srep22432"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cho, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-ion Storage Performances of FeSe<sub>x</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Hollow Nanoparticles-Decorated Reduced Graphene Oxide Balls Prepared by Nanoscale Kirkendall Diffusion</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an attractive alternative to lithium-ion batteries that alleviate problems with lithium availability and cost.  Despite several studies of cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries involving layered oxide materials, there are few low-voltage metal oxide anodes capable of operating sodium ion reversibly at room temp.  We have synthesized amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube electrodes directly grown on current collectors without binders and additives to use as an anode for sodium-ion batteries.  We find that only amorphous large diam. nanotubes (&gt;80 nm I.D.) can support electrochem. cycling with sodium ions.  These electrodes maximize their capacity in operando and reach reversible capacity of 150 mA-h/g in 15 cycles.  We also demonstrate for the first time a full cell all-oxide sodium-ion battery using amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube anode coupled to a Na1.0Li0.2Ni0.25Mn0.75Oδ cathode at room temp. exhibiting good rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr8q2bDG7YJCbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhH-acJgo8vdg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1ChtLbP&amp;md5=66a2a71991a01d6823c9c01024f65c74</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b02413"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mao, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mignerey, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solid-State Fabrication of SnS<sub>2</sub>/C Nanospheres for High-Performance Sodium Ion Battery Anode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin disulfide (SnS2) has emerged as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (NIBs) due to its unique layered structure, high theor. capacity, and low cost.  Conventional SnS2 nanomaterials are normally synthesized using hydrothermal method, which is time-consuming and difficult to scale up for mass prodn.  In this study, we develop a simple solid-state reaction method, in which the carbon-coated SnS2 (SnS2/C) anode materials were synthesized by annealing metallic Sn, sulfur powder, and polyacrylonitrile in a sealed vacuum glass tube.                         rightTab-cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A rationally designed dual role anode material for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries: case study of eco-friendly Fe3O4</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hariharan, Srirama; Saravanan, Kuppan; Ramar, Vishwanathan; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2945-2953</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PPCPFQ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Identifying dual role electrode materials capable of storing both lithium and sodium are thought to be highly relevant, as these materials could find potential applications simultaneously in lithium- and sodium-ion batteries.  In this regard, the concept of dual alkali storage is demonstrated in Fe3O4 anode material undergoing conversion reaction.  To enable improved storage, a rational active material and electrode design is proposed.  Accordingly, the following features were simultaneously incorporated into the design: (a) an optimal particle size, (b) a conducting matrix, (c) adequately large active material surface area and (d) strong electrode material-current collector integrity.  Electrodes incorporating this rational design exhibit excellent high-rate performance and impressive cyclability during lithium storage.  For instance, Fe3O4 electrodes deliver a charge capacity of 950 mA-h/g at 1.2C (∼2.6 times higher than graphite and 5.4 times higher than Li4Ti5O12).  Further, these electrodes show no signs of capacity fade even up to 1100 cycles.  Impressively, the cells could also be charged-discharged to 65% of their theor. capacity in just 5 min or 12C (11.11 A/g).  The rate performance and cyclability of lithium storage achieved here are amongst the highest reported values in the literature for the conversion reaction in Fe3O4.  Besides lithium storage, the dual role of this anode is shown by demonstrating its sodium storage ability by conversion reaction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq1Ci_Jjiz4hrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhH-acJgo8vdg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvVChu70%253D&amp;md5=3227d1451a01a4a00d2e9d504da1dc9e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b04178"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kalubarme, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon Encapsulated Tin Oxide Nanocomposites: An Efficient Anode for High Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The major obstacle in realizing sodium (Na)-ion batteries (NIBs) is the absence of suitable neg. electrodes.  This is because graphite, a com. well known anode material for lithium-ion batteries, cannot be utilized as an insertion host for Na ions due to its large ionic size.  In this study, a simple and cost-effective hydrothermal method to prep. carbon coated tin oxide (SnO2) nanostructures as an efficient anode material for NIBs was reported as a function of the solvent used.  A single phase SnO2 resulted for the ethanol solvent, while a blend of SnO and SnO2 resulted for the DI water and ethylene glycol solvents.  The elemental mapping in the transmission electron microscopy confirmed the presence of carbon coating on the SnO2 nanoparticles.  In cell tests, the anodes of carbon coated SnO2 prepd. in ethanol solvent exhibited stable cycling performance and attained a capacity of about 514 mAh g-1 on the first charge.  With the help of the conductive carbon coating, the SnO2 delivers more capacity at high rates: 304 mAh g-1 at the 1 C rate, 213 mAh g-1 at the 2 C rate and 133 mAh g-1 at the 5 C rate.  The excellent cyclability and high rate capability are the result of the formation of a mixed conducting network and uniform carbon coating on the SnO2 nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoqatmxHHS-GLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljmqzq99FCAIg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFyqs7zL&amp;md5=f5816e29156cc8b7ab64982328e0b5a2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b06590"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ Synthesis of MnS Hollow Microspheres on Reduced Graphene Oxide Sheets as High-Capacity and Long-Life Anodes for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. The MnS/RGO composite material was used as the anode for Na-ion batteries for the first time and exhibited excellent cycling performance, superior specific capacity, and great cycle stability and rate capability for both Li- and Na-ion batteries.  Compared with nonencapsulated pure MnS hollow microspheres, these MnS/RGO nanocomposites demonstrated excellent charge-discharge stability and long cycle life. Addnl., this electrode architecture can be up-scaled and thus should hold a position in the future low-cost, high-rate and ultralong-life next-generation energy storage devices.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, to create efficient charge transfer, we propose a 3D hierarchical meso- and macroporous NVP-based hybrid cathode concept with connected Na ion/electron pathways for ultrafast charge and discharge NIBs, consisting of NVP nanocrystals coated with amorphous carbon and then wrapped by reduced graphene oxide nanosheets (abbreviated as NVP@C@rGO).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transitional metal oxides are promising anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to their high theor. capacities and material abundance; however, their sodium storage capability is significantly hindered by the sluggish sodiation/desodiation reaction kinetics.  Herein, towards achieving fast and durable sodiation/desodiation reaction, Fe3O4 and Co3O4 nanocrystals encapsulated in carbon micro-spheres are synthesized via a biochem. approach using recombinant elastin-like polypeptides contg. hexahistidine tag (ELP16-His) followed by annealing.  Fe3O4 and Co3O4 nanocrystals of approx. 5 nm in size, which are uniformly dispersed in a carbon matrix, are obtained.  The carbon-encapsulated metal oxides exhibit encouraging sodium storage capacities (657 and 246 mA h g-1 at 0.1 and 2 A g-1, resp., for carbon-encapsulated Fe3O4; 583 and 183 mA h g-1 at 0.1 and 2 A g-1, resp., for carbon-encapsulated Co3O4), and have a high capacity retention after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries are one of the realistic promising alternatives to the Li analogs.  However, neither theor. energy/power d. nor the practical values reach the values of Li cathodes.  Poorer performance is expected owing to larger size, larger mass, and lower cell voltage.  Nonetheless, Na ion batteries are considered to be practically relevant in view of the abundance of the element Na.  The arguments in favor of Li and to the disadvantage of Na would be completely obsolete if the specific performance data of the latter would match the 1st.  Here the authors present a cathode consisting of C-coated nanosized Na3V2(PO4)3 embedded in a porous C matrix, which not only matches but even out-shines Li cathodes under high rate conditions.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cube-shaped porous C (CPC) was obtained from the carbonization of MOF-5 (Zn4O(OOCC6H4COO)3) crystals and shows abundant micro/mesopores, high mech. strength, largest surface area (2316 m2 g-1, BET method) and good elec. cond.                         rightTab-cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MnFe2O4@C Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Yu, Chuanming; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnFe2O4 nanodots (∼3.3 nm) homogeneously dispersed in porous nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (denoted as MFO@C) were prepd. by a feasible electrospinning technique.  Meanwhile, MFO@C with the character of flexible free-standing membrane was directly used as binder- and current collector-free anode for sodium-ion batteries, exhibiting high electrochem. performance with high-rate capability (305 mA h g-1 at 10000 mA g-1 in comparison of 504 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1) and ultralong cycling life (ca. 90% capacity retention after 4200 cycles).  The Na-storage mechanism was systematically studied, revealing that MnFe2O4 is converted into metallic Mn and Fe after the first discharge (MnFe2O4 + 8Na+ + 8e- → Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O) and then to MnO and Fe2O3 during the following charge (Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O → MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e-).  The subsequent cycles occur through reversible redox reactions of MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e- &lt;-&gt; Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O, of which the redn./oxidn. of MnO/Mn takes place at a lower potential than that of Fe2O3/Fe.  Furthermore, a soft package sodium-ion full battery with MFO@C anode and Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C cathode was assembled, delivering a stable capacity of ∼400 mA h g-1 for MFO@C (with 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1) and a promising energy d. of 77.8 Wh kg-1 for the whole battery.  This is owing to the distinctive structure of very-fine MnFe2O4 nanodots embedded in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers, which effectively improves the utilization rate of active materials, facilitates the transportation of electrons and Na+ ions, and prevents the particle pulverization/agglomeration upon prolonged cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo_fovS2KMexbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljAfpgl6elDdg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XlsFKqtLk%253D&amp;md5=1f0fa2211d961158137c8cc4eb8fdd4c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2014.10.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospinning Preparation of Ultra-Long Aligned Nanofibers Thin Films for High Performance Fully Flexible Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">12</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">339</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">346</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) are of increasing interest as mobile power supply for the next-generation of flexible electronics.  The current flexible LIBs are generally limited by relatively poor ductility, short cycle-life and low charge and discharge rate.  Herein, we report a rational design and prepn. of flexible ultra-long, aligned carbon nanofibers thin films with embedded In2O3 nanocrystals (In2O3@FUACNFF) as a binder free anode for highly flexible LIBs.  In this work, needleless electrospinning has been demonstrated to be to an effective method for the prepn. of In2O3@FUACNFF with super-high throughput.  The In2O3@FUACNFF can ensure excellent charge transport, electrolyte transport and mech. flexibility, thus leading to excellent electrochem. performance and exceptional flexibility.  The In2O3@FUACNFF exhibited excellent cycling ability even after 500 cycles, with a capacity of 545.6 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 and rate performance even at the highest c.d. of 100 A g-1 with a reversible capacity of 224.2 mA h g-1.  Moreover, highly flexible full batteries were also fabricated to demonstrate the superior durability (the elec. stability of the manufd. flexible full battery was hardly affected after more than 120 times folding cycles), excellent cycle-ability (the capacity retention was almost 100% in the measured range from the 17th cycle on) and high rate performance (321.4 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 1000 mA g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_iwgeMmDlIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljAfpgl6elDdg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this communication, we report a needleless electrospinning setup using an electriferous rotating cone as the spinneret.  The typical prodn. rate by this method is about 10 g per min, which is 1000 times more than that of the traditional electrospinning method.  Nanofibers could be obtained as highly aligned arrays with lengths up to several centimeters by modifying the collector.  In addn., we found that it was the value of the voltage between the cone and the collector that affected the diam. of the electrospinning fibers.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A simple and scalable electrospinning process followed by thermal treatment was used to fabricate carbon nanofibers.  The as-prepd. carbon nanofibers were investigated as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Remarkably, due to their weakly ordered turbostratic structure and a large interlayer spacing between graphene sheets, the carbon nanofibers exhibit a dominant adsorption/insertion sodium storage mechanism that shows high reversibility.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In attempt to reduce the amt. of toxic Co in cobalt oxides, NiCoMnO4 nanoparticles were synthesized via a facile hydrothermal route and their electrochem. properties have been investigated as a novel electrode material for supercapacitors.  Samples have been characterized using X-ray diffraction (XRD), energy dispersive X-ray anal. (EDAX), and XPS.  N2 adsorption/desorption measurements demonstrated a high sp. surface area of 175 m2 g-1.  The morphol. of the samples has been probed with scanning (SEM) and transmission (TEM) electron microscopy.  The electrochem. properties of the NiCoMnO4 nanoparticles have been evaluated as electrode materials for energy storage application by means of various electrochem. techniques including cyclic voltammetry, galvanostatic charge-discharge measurements, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  According to the obtained results, the NiCoMnO4 electrodes showed significant improved capacitive performance in comparison with pure oxides (e.g. NiO, Co3O4, and Mn3O4).  The NiCoMnO4 electrodes with a high mass loading of ∼10 mg cm-2 exhibited a high specific capacitance of 510 F g-1 at 1 A g-1, and a desirable rate capability (retaining 285 F g-1 at 10 A g-1).  Finally, asym. devices based on NiCoMnO4 nanoparticles as pos. electrodes and reduced graphene oxide nanosheets as neg. electrodes were assembled, showing a remarkable performance including high energy (20 W h kg-1), and stunning power d.(37.5 kW kg-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYIuamQcCPRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-7RYmgJBi9A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XktVOqtLo%253D&amp;md5=9a0a6142a7c63863868fe99240a567e1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b11022"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Novel and Facile One-Pot Solvothermal Synthesis of PEDOT-PSS/Ni-Mn-Co-O Hybrid as an Advanced Supercapacitor Electrode Material</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Novel and Facile One-Pot Solvothermal Synthesis of PEDOT-PSS/Ni-Mn-Co-O Hybrid as an Advanced Supercapacitor Electrode Material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Chengjie; Yang, Chunming; Jiang, Min; Deng, Cuifen; Yang, Lishan; Li, Junhua; Qian, Dong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, a novel and facile one-pot method has been developed for the synthesis of a hybrid consisting of Ni-Mn-Co ternary oxide and poly(3,4-ethylenedioxythiophene)-polystyrenesulfonate (PEDOT-PSS/NMCO) with a hierarchical three-dimensional net structure via a solvothermal-copptn. coupled with oxidative polymn. route.  Apart from the achievement of polymn., copptn., and solvothermal in one pot, the hydroxyl (OH-) ions generated from the oxidative polymn. of org. monomer by neutral KMnO4 soln. were skillfully employed as precipitants for metal ions.  As compared with the PEDOT-PSS/Ni-Mn binary oxide, PEDOT-PSS/Co-Mn binary oxide, and PEDOT-PSS/MnO2, PEDOT-PSS1.5/NMCO exhibits overwhelmingly superior supercapacitive performance, more specifically, a high specific capacitance of 1234.5 F g-1 at a c.d. of 1 A g-1, a good capacitance retention of 83.7% at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1 after 1000 cycles, an energy d. of 51.9 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 275 W kg-1, and an energy d. of 21.4 W h kg-1 at an extremely elevated power d. of 5500 W kg-1.  Noticeably, the energy d. and power d. of PEDOT-PSS/NMCO are by far higher than those of the existing analogs recently reported.  The exceptional performance of PEDOT-PSS/NMCO benefits from its unique mesoporous architecture, which could provide a larger reaction surface area, faster ion and electron transfer ability, and good structural stability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">With a logical management of the catalyst selectivity, we present a scalable, membraneless alk. direct liq. fuel cell (DLFC) platform.  The uniqueness of this innovation is that the inexpensive (non-platinum) cathode catalysts, based on strongly coupled transition-metal-oxide nanocrystals and nano-structured carbon materials (e. g., NiCo2O4 nano-particles on a nitrogen-doped graphene and MnNiCoO4 nano-particles on a nitrogen-doped multi-wall carbon nanotube), exhibit high activity for the oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) but without activity for the anode fuel oxidn. reaction (FOR).  Therefore, operation of the DLFCs allows the anode fuel to freely enter the cathode.  This strategy avoids the reliance on expensive or difficult-to-develop cation- or anion-exchange membranes and circumvents the scalability concerns of the conventional membraneless DLFCs that are operated under a laminar-flow principle.  With proper catalyst selectivity, a variety of org. liqs. can be used as anode fuels.  The high power d. delivered by the membraneless DLFCs with inexpensive components and safe fuels can enable the development of not only small-scale portable power sources but also large-scale energy generation systems for transportation and stationary storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqfBV1_WylSKrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-7RYmgJBi9A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFaqsb7K&amp;md5=c937172a6dd7f7d8ec699d60438942b8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Mn-Co-Ni-O ultrafine ceramic nanoparticles are successfully synthesized by the reverse microemulsion method in a triton X-100/n-hexanol/cyclohexane system.  The thermal decompn. process, crystallinity and crystal structure of Mn-Co-Ni-O powders are investigated and characterized by thermogravimetric-differential scanning calorimetry (TG/DSC), Fourier Transform IR (FT-IR), X-ray powders diffraction (XRD) and High Resoln.                         rightTab-cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of metal oxide/reduced graphene oxide hybrids with high lithium storage capacity and stable cyclability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Jixin; Zhu, Ting; Zhou, Xiaozhu; Zhang, Yanyan; Lou, Xiong Wen; Chen, Xiaodong; Zhang, Hua; Hng, Huey Hoon; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report an environment-friendly approach to synthesize transition metal oxide nanoparticles (NPs)/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) sheets hybrids by combining the redn. of graphene oxide (GO) with the growth of metal oxide NPs in one step.  Either Fe2O3 or CoO NPs were grown onto rGO sheets in EtOH soln. through a solvothermal process, during which GOs were reduced to rGO without the addn. of any strong reducing agent, e.g. hydrazine, or requiring any post-high-temp. annealing process.  The GO or rGO during the pptn. of metal oxide NPs may act as heterogeneous nucleation seeds to facilitate the formation of small crystal grains.  This may allow more efficient diffusion of Li ions and lead to high specific capacities.  These metal oxide NPs-rGO hybrids were used as anodes for Li-ion batteries, which showed high capacities and excellent charge-discharge cycling stability in the voltage window between 0.01 and 3.0 V.  For example, Fe2O3 NPs/rGO hybrids showed specific capacity of 881 mA h g-1 in the 90th cycle at a discharge c.d. of 302 mA g-1 (0.3 C), while CoO NPs/rGO hybrids showed a lower capacity of 600 mA h g-1 in the 90th cycle at a discharge c.d. of 215 mA g-1 (0.3 C).  These nanohybrids also show excellent capacities at high C rate currents, e.g. 611 mA h g-1 for Fe2O3/rGO sample in the 300th cycle at 2014 mA g-1 (2 C).  Such synthesis technique can be a promising route to produce advanced electrode materials for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXP25LIQ9WI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie_PhcqufEcA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXjtlSgsL8%253D&amp;md5=e66e6e6cb05f91e9a6f365cd23a241e8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref56" class="rightTabRefNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit56" data-doi="10.1039/c1ee02168k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cong, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A General Strategy toward Graphene@Metal Oxide Core-Shell Nanostructures for High-Performance Lithium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         rightTab-cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A facile route to synthesize multiporous MnCo2O4 and CoMn2O4 spinel quasi-hollow spheres with improved lithium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jingfa; Xiong, Shenglin; Li, Xiaowei; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile and general way for the synthesis of porous and hollow complex oxides is highly desirable owing to their significant applications for energy storage and other fields.  In this contribution, uniform Mn0.33Co0.67CO3 and Co0.33Mn0.67CO3 microspheres are firstly fabricated solvothermally just by tuning the molar ratio of Mn and Co.  Subsequently, the growth of multiporous MnCo2O4 and CoMn2O4 quasi-hollow microspheres by topotactic chem. transformation from the corresponding precursors are realized through a non-equil. heat treatment process.  Topotactic conversion further demonstrated that the much larger CoMn2O4 pores than those of MnCo2O4 are possibly due to the longer transfer distance of ions.  When evaluated as anode materials for LIBs (lithium ion batteries), after 25 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1, the resultant MnCo2O4 and CoMn2O4 quasi-hollow microspheres possessed reversible capacities of 755 and 706 mA h g-1, resp.  In particular, the MnCo2O4 samples could deliver a reversible capacity as high as 610 mA h g-1 even at a higher c.d. of 400 mA g-1 with excellent electrochem. stability after 100 cycles of testing, indicating its potential application in LIBs.  We believe that such good performance results from the appropriate pore size and quasi-hollow nature of MnCo2O4 microspheres, which can effectively buffer the large vol. variation of anodes based on the conversion reaction during Li+ insertion/extn.  The present strategy is simple but very effective, and due to its versatility, it can be extended to other binary, even ternary complex metal oxides with high-performance in LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrbhvspDIEXS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie_PhcqufEcA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXis1Chtb0%253D&amp;md5=6077ea996d47a6809543d23637a09546</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref58" class="rightTabRefNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit58" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.01.105"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qin, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Microspheres Derived from Oatmeal as High Capacity and Superior Long Life Anode Material for Sodium Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         rightTab-cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped carbon microspheres derived from oatmeal as high capacity and superior long life anode material for sodium ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Dong; Yu, Caiyan; Zhang, Xiaojie; Qin, Wei; Lu, Ting; Hu, Bingwen; Li, Huili; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">191</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped C microspheres (NCSs) derived from oatmeal are employed as anodes for Na ion batteries (SIBs).  Their morphol., structure and electrochem. performance were characterized by field emission SEM, x-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, XPS, N adsorption-desorption isotherms, galvanostatic charge/discharge tests, cyclic voltammetry and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, resp.  NCSs treated at 500° exhibit a high max. charge capacity of 336 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 and even at a high c.d. of 10 A g-1 within 70 s charging time, a capacity of 104 mA h g-1 is maintained after 12500 cycles without obvious decay.  The high capacity, excellent rate performance, long life cycling and ultrafast rechargeable ability enable the NCSs to be a promising candidate for practical SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoMLNKZGaDv-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liRtfN4vwzM1Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtlWjtbc%253D&amp;md5=27ba87f782244e7692481a3e78d2d55d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref59" class="rightTabRefNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit59" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE00941G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultra-Thick Graphene Bulk Supercapacitor Electrodes for Compact Energy Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">9</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3135</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C6EE00941G</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-thick graphene bulk supercapacitor electrodes for compact energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Huan; Tao, Ying; Zheng, Xiaoyu; Luo, Jiayan; Kang, Feiyu; Cheng, Hui-Ming; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3135-3142</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Compact energy storage with high volumetric performance is highly important.  However, the state-of-the-art electrodes and devices remain far from the requirements due to the lack of consideration from a device perspective, which not only demands a high specific gravimetric capacity, but also needs to take into account operation voltage, material d. and electrode thickness.  We develop a novel approach to fabricate a monolithic ultra-thick and dense carbon electrode for sym. supercapacitors, starting with graphene assembly and taking all the above factors into consideration.  We found that zinc chloride is an ideal sacrificial pore former, and taken together with capillary drying can tune the sp. surface area of the monolithic graphene from 370 to over 1000 m2 g-1 while the monoliths maintain a high d. from 1.6 to 0.6 g cm-3.  Having a good balance of porosity and d., the directly sliced graphene pellet electrode with a thickness up to 400 μm delivers a capacitance of 150 F cm-3 in an ionic liq. electrolyte, corresponding to a volumetric energy d. of ∼65 W h L-1 for a sym. supercapacitor device, the highest value reported to date for supercapacitors.  This study presents a design principle for electrode materials towards next-generation energy storage devices, not limited to supercapacitors, which are becoming smaller, lighter but more energetic.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoAQiQ3Is7rb7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liRtfN4vwzM1Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XotF2qtrs%253D&amp;md5=b1d91a6572e5f1cc75a750fea90da967</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref60" class="rightTabRefNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit60" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Augustyn, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Come, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lowe, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tolbert, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Abruña, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Simon, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dunn, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Rate Electrochemical Energy Storage through LiC Intercalation Pseudocapacitance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">12</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">518</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">522</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/nmat3601</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">518-522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liRtfN4vwzM1Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref61" class="rightTabRefNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit61" data-doi="10.1021/jp074464w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Polleux, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lim, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dunn, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO<sub>2</sub> (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Phys. Chem. C</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2007</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">111</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">14925</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">14931</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jp074464w</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO2 (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, John; Polleux, Julien; Lim, James; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2007</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">111</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14925-14931</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages of using nanostructured materials for electrochem. energy storage have focused on the benefits assocd. with short path lengths.  However, another contribution, capacitive effects which become increasingly important at nanoscale dimensions, was studied.  Nanocryst. TiO2 (anatase) was studied over a dimensional regime where both capacitive and Li intercalation processes contribute to the total stored charge.  An anal. of the voltammetric sweep data was used to distinguish between the amt. of charge stored by these 2 processes.  At particle sizes &lt;10 nm, capacitive contributions became increasingly important, leading to greater amts. of total stored charge (gravimetrically normalized) with decreasing TiO2 particle size.  The area normalized capacitance is well &gt;100 μF/cm2, confirming that the capacitive contribution was pseudocapacitive.  Also, decreasing the particle size to the nanoscale regime led to faster charge/discharge rates because diffusion-controlled Li ion intercalation was replaced by faradaic reactions which occur at the surface of the material.  The charge storage and kinetic benefits derived from using nanoscale metal oxides provide an interesting direction for the design of materials that offer both power d. and energy d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0ueeFhvSDZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liRtfN4vwzM1Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXhtVChs7zL&amp;md5=b47809cb86f6cf28f5758e0eb3eac71e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref62" class="rightTabRefNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit62" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201404472"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lin, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fast and Large Lithium Storage in 3D Porous VN Nanowires-Graphene Composite as a Superior Anode toward High-Performance Hybrid Supercapacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Funct. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">25</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2270</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2278</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201404472</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fast and Large Lithium Storage in 3D Porous VN Nanowires-Graphene Composite as a Superior Anode Toward High-Performance Hybrid Supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Rutao; Lang, Junwei; Zhang, Peng; Lin, Zongyuan; Yan, Xingbin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2270-2278</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-ion hybrid capacitors (LIHCs), consisting of an energy-type redox anode and a power-type double-layer cathode, are attracting significant attention due to the good combination with the advantages of conventional Li-ion batteries and supercapacitors.  However, most anodes are battery-like materials with the sluggish kinetics of Li-ion storage, which seriously restrict the energy storage of LIHCs at the high charge/discharge rates.  Herein, vanadium nitride (VN) nanowire is demonstrated to have obvious pseudocapacitive characteristic of Li-ion storage and can get further gains in energy storage through a 3D porous architecture with the assistance of conductive reduced graphene oxide (RGO).  The as-prepd. 3D VN-RGO composite exhibits the large Li-ion storage capacity and fast charge/discharge rate within a wide working widow from 0.01-3 V (vs. Li/Li+), which could potentially boost the operating potential and the energy and power densities of LIHCs.  By employing such 3D VN-RGO composite and porous carbon nanorods with a high surface area of 3343 m2 g-1 as the anode and cathode, resp., a novel LIHCs is fabricated with an ultrahigh energy d. of 162 Wh kg-1 at 200 W kg-1, which also remains 64 Wh kg-1 even at a high power d. of 10 kW kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoVXl_sHI4udrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liRtfN4vwzM1Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvF2gtLY%253D&amp;md5=cb9a635333a988e76063378327023ab7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref63" class="rightTabRefNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit63" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2003.10.016"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jow, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Impedance Study on the Low Temperature of Li-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2004</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">49</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1057</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1061</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2003.10.016</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical impedance study on the low temperature of Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, S. S.; Xu, K.; Jow, T. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2004</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1057-1061</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cycling performance of Li-ion batteries was studied by using electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  Results showed that total resistance of the Li-ion batteries is mainly composed of bulk resistance (Rb), solid-state interface resistance (Rsei) and charge-transfer resistance (Rct).  During cycling, the Rb and Rsei do not change while the Rct displays two min. in the same voltage regions where the major peaks of differential capacities are present.  The Rct can be linked to kinetics of the battery electrochem. reaction.  In response to the temp. change, the Rb and Rsei vary in a very similar manner, while the Rct shows significant difference.  In the fully charged and discharged states as well as at the low temps. (≤20°), the total resistance of the Li-ion batteries is predominated by the Rct.  Using the term of the Rct, we explained two low-temp. phenomena of the Li-ion battery: (a) charging of a fully discharged battery is much more difficult than discharging of a fully charged battery, and (b) both the power (operating voltage) and energy (delivered capacity) are substantially reduced.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplYUwg57Nby7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liRtfN4vwzM1Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2cXmtFWmsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=1be699464091e1d4ed024d22eb3540bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref64" class="rightTabRefNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit64" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2011.02.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Manivannan, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cyclability Study of Silicon-Carbon Composite Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries Using Electrochemical Impedance Spectroscopy</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         rightTab-cas_cit64R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">64</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cyclability study of silicon-carbon composite anodes for lithium-ion batteries using electrochemical impedance spectroscopy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Juchen; Sun, Ann; Chen, Xilin; Wang, Chunsheng; Manivannan, Ayyakkannu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">56</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3981-3987</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The effects of carbonization process and C nanofiber/nanotube additives on the cycling stability of Si-C composite anodes were studied by monitoring the impedance evolution during charge/discharge cycles with electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS).  Three types of Si-C anodes were studied: the 1st type consisted of Si nanoparticles incorporated into a network of C nanofibers (CNFs) and multi-walled C nanotubes (MWNTs), with annealed polymer binder.  The 2nd type of Si-C anodes was prepd. by further heat treatment of the 1st Si-C anodes to carbonize the polymer binder.  The 3rd Si-C anode was as same as the 2nd one except no CNFs and MWNTs being added.  Impedance anal. revealed that the carbonization process stabilized the Si-C anode structure and decreased the charge transfer resistance, thus improving the cycling stability.  However, although the MWNTs/CNFs additives could enhance the electronic cond. of the Si-C anodes, the induced inhomogeneous structure decreased the integrity of the electrode, resulting in a poor long term cycling stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8R3BLiB75k7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limyzErk87Afw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXkslCnsbk%253D&amp;md5=8a1f09ef0a807a6aed6d3e345e2814f2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref65"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref65" class="rightTabRefNumLink">65</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit65" data-doi="10.1002/9780470381588"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Orazem, M. (function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){

<script nonce="90da8c58cddeb325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8c58cddeb325-SJC">

	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {

)|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>

var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
